-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_activator.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'activator'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['protein' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'promoter' ,'transcription' ,'rna_polymerase_rna_p' ,'chromatin' ,'eukaryota' ,'repressor']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="activator">Activator</a> - A [protein](#protein) that binds [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) and [promotes](#promoter) the [transcription](#transcription) of nearby [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) (often directionally, on one side of the binding site, but sometimes bidirectionally). An activator can do this by recruiting [RNA polymerase (RNA-P)](#rna_polymerase_rna_p), opening a cell's [chromatin](#chromatin) allowing access to the [promoter](#promoter) region by [RNA-P](#rna_polymerase_rna_p) (in [eukaryota](#eukaryota)). This blocks a [repressor](#repressor) from binding.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_agar.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'agar'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['agarose' ,'agarophytes' ,'rhodophyta' ,'phylum' ,'agaropectin' ,'electrophoresis']
linkedFrom: ['agaropectin','agarose','cell_culture']
---

<a id="agar">Agar</a> - Agar, not to be confused with [agarose](#agarose) is a jelly like substance extracted from red algae known as [agarophytes](#agarophytes) in the [Rhodophyta](#rhodophyta) [phylum](#phylum). Agar is a mixture composed of about 30% [agaropectin](#agaropectin) and 70% [agarose](#agarose) (used in [electrophoretic gels](#electrophoresis)). Agar is used as a solid medium for microbiology.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_ahl.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'ahl'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['molecule' ,'diffusion' ,'quorum_sensing' ,'signal' ,'bacterial_colony' ,'concentration' ,'bacteria' ,'transcription_factor_tf' ,'lux_system_luxi_luxr' ,'repressor' ,'promoter']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="ahl">AHL</a> - They are a class of homoserine lactones with an acyl group. These are small [molecules](#molecule) that can [diffuse](#diffusion) between cells. They typically act as a [quorum sensing](#quorum_sensing) and [signaling molecule](#signal) as it can [diffuse](#diffusion) throughout a [bacterial population](#bacterial_colony) such that the knowledge of the [concentration](#concentration) of the AHL is shared between all [bacteria](#bacteria). The [bacteria](#bacteria) can detect the AHL [concentration](#concentration) by way of a [transcription factor](#transcription_factor_tf) that can bind and be modulated by the AHL molecule. For example, the [LuxI gene](#lux_system_luxi_luxr) produces an AHL that can then bind [LuxR](#lux_system_luxi_luxr), relieving its [repressor](#repressor) on the corresponding [promoter](#promoter).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_agaropectin.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'agaropectin'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['agar']
linkedFrom: ['agar']
---

<a id="agaropectin">Agaropectin</a> - One of the two main components of [agar](#agar), composing about 30%, mainly composed of D-glucuronic acid and pyruvic acid.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="agarophytes">Agarophytes</a> - A seeweed typically a red algae. It can be used in biological experiments and for use in the creation of cell cultures.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_agarose.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'agarose'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['agar' ,'electrophoresis' ,'chromatography']
linkedFrom: ['agar']
---

<a id="agarose">Agarose</a> - Agarose is a sugar or polysaccharide. It is a main component of [agar](#agar), which is used a solid medium for microbial cultures. Agarose is used alone for the separation of DNA fragments in [electrophoretic gels](#electrophoresis) and [chromatographic](#chromatography) protein purification.

Molecular structure of the Agarose molecule.

 The chemical composition of agarose is C12H18O9, and its molecular weight is 306.2659 g/mol.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_a_alginate.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'alginate'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'biochemistry'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['cell_wall']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="alginate">Alginate</a> - Component of the [cell walls](#cell_wall) of many rhodophytes and kelps. Alginates have an affinity for water, and so help to slow dessication when the algae are exposed to the air; they are commercially important in the production of paper, toothpaste, beer, and frozen foods.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_allosteric-regulation.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'allosteric-regulation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['conformation' ,'protein' ,'enzyme' ,'molecule' ,'transcription_factor_tf' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="allosteric_regulation">Allosteric Regulation</a> - Allosteric regulation happens when a [conformational change](#conformation) (the allosteric part) affects the function of a [protein](#protein) or [enzyme](#enzyme). For example, a small [molecule](#molecule) may bind a [transcription factor](#transcription_factor_tf) and cause a [conformational change](#conformation) that removes the [TF](#transcription_factor_tf)'s ability to bind [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid), rendering it inactive.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_alpha-helix.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'alpha-helix'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['amino_acid' ,'secondary_structure' ,'betaSheet']
linkedFrom: ['motif','secondary_structure']
---

<a id="alpha_helix">Alpha Helix</a> - An alpha helix is an [amino acid](#amino_acid) sequence pattern that results in a [secondary structure](#secondary_structure) in the form of a right handed helix. This helix is created by the donation of a hydrogen bond from the backbone N-H groups to the C=O groups. These interactions happen on average every three to four [amino acids](#amino_acid) in a sequence, with about 13 atoms involved in one ring. See also [Î²-sheet](#betaSheet).

Human growth hormon cartoon rendition, depicting various alpha helices.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="alphavirus">Alphavirus</a> - Small, spherical, [enveloped viruses](#enveloped_virus) with a genome of a single [positive (sense) RNA](#positive_rna_rna) strand. Ahphaviruses have been engineered into self replicating [RNA](#rna) and are commonly referred to as replicons.

linksTo: ['']

---

<a id="amniote">Amniote</a> - Any of a group of land-dwelling vertebrates that have an amnion during embryonic development, including reptiles, birds, and mammals. Most extant mammals give live birth, the "egg" is retained inside the body during gestation; in humans the equivalent is known as amniotic sac.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_anneal.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'anneal'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_assembly' ,'complementary' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'secondary_structure' ,'inhibitor' ,'molecule' ,'hydrogenBond' ,'denature']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="anneal">Anneal</a> - In the context of [DNA assembly](#dna_assembly) this means the coming together of [complementary](#complementary) (or [near-complementary](#complementary), in some cases) sequences of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). This is often assisted by a change in temperature: two [complementary sequences](#complementary) are often heated up (to say 95Â°C) and then allowed to cool down. The heating removes self-annealing, which causes [secondary structures](#secondary_structure) to form in the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid), which might [inhibit](#inhibitor) annealing to the other [molecule](#molecule). The cooling down allows the formation of [hydrogen bonds](#hydrogenBond) between the two [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) strands. The opposite process to annealing is melting or [denaturing](#denature) of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid), which happens at high temperatures.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="antibiotic_resistance_gene">Antibiotic Resistance Gene</a> - These [genes](#gene) create a product that confers antibiotic resistance. For example, KanR confers resistance to the antibiotic kanamycin. This is often used for [selection](#selection) of microorganisms or others.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_antibody.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'antibody'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['bacteria' ,'virus']
linkedFrom: ['epitope_antigenic_determinant','immunogenicity','southern_blot','western_blot_immunoblot']
---

<a id="antibody">Antibody</a> - Also known as an immunoglobulin (Ig), is a large, Y-shaped protein produced mainly by plasma cells that is used by the immune system to identify and neutralise pathogens such as [bacteria](#bacteria) and [viruses](#virus). The average size of an antibody is about 10 nm in length (Reth 2013: Nature Immunology - Matching cellular dimensions with molecular sizes) and its molecular weight would be about 150 kDa (Padlan EA. Anatomy of the antibody molecule. Mol. Immunol. 1994;31:169-217).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="antigen">Antigen</a> - Any biological or [synthetic](#synthetic) molecule which causes an [immune response](#immuneSystem) when introduced into the body and is capable of reacting with the products of the [immune system](#immuneSystem).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_antigenic-determinant.mdx'

word: 'antigenic-determinant'

<a id="antisense_sequence">Antisense Sequence</a> - A sequence of [nucleotides](#nucleotide) complementary to a [sense coding sequence](#sense_sequence), which may be either the strand of a [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) that undergoes [transcription](#transcription), or a [messenger RNA molecule](#mrna).

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_apoptosis.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'apoptosis'

---

<a id="apoptosis">Apoptosis</a> - The process of preprogrammed [cell](#cell) death which occurs in [multicellular](#multicellular) organisms. Do not confuse with [necrosis](#necrosis), which is caused by trauma. Apoptosis is a normal part of an organisms physiology.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_aptamer.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'aptamer'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['rna' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'ligand' ,'specificity' ,'conformation']
linkedFrom: ['ligand']
---

<a id="aptamer">Aptamer</a> - A sequence of [RNA](#rna) (or sometimes [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid)) that folds into a particular 3D structure, enabling it to bind some [ligand molecule](#ligand), *exempli gratia* caffeine, with high [specificity](#specificity) and strength. Binding of the [ligand](#ligand) can sometimes induce a [conformational change](#conformation) in the aptamer, which can be used as a signal for the binding event in the case of aptamer-based circuits.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_association-constant-binding-constant.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'association-constant-binding-constant'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dissociation_constant']
linkedFrom: ['dissociation_constant']
---

<a id="association_constant_binding_constant">Association Constant (Binding constant)</a> - A special case of the equilibrium constant *K*. It is the inverse of the [dissociation constant](#dissociation_constant). It describes the binding and unbinding of a receptor (R) and a ligand (L).

 $$ R + L \leftrightarrows RL $$ $$ K_a = \frac{k_{on}}{k_{off}} = \frac{\[RL\]}{\[R\]\[L\]} $$

 See also [dissociation constant](#dissociation_constant).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_a_atp-adenosine-triphosphate.mdx'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="atp_adenosine_triphosphate">ATP (Adenosine Triphosphate)</a> - The primary molecule used by living organisms as fuel. ATP is relatively stable, high energy molecule used to fuel chemical reactions within cells.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_attenuation.mdx'

<a id="attenuation">Attenuation</a> - To lessen or weaken the effect of something. For example, noise in a system can be attenuated with certain techniques, such as feedback, which can reduce the amount of noise or lessen its effect on the system.

-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_a_autoregulation.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'autoregulation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['geneExpression']
linkedFrom: ['feedback','motif']
---

<a id="autoregulation">Autoregulation</a> - Self-regulation. *exempli gratia*, an electric heater may employ negative autoregulation in order to keep a steady temperature in the room. If it heats the room too much, the room gets hot; a temperature sensor detects this and turns the heater off. Once the room cools down, the sensor detects this event as well and turns the heater on. The heater regulates itself in this way. [Gene expression](#geneExpression) is also autoregulatory; products regulate the expression of the gene (itself).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_ecology_a_autotroph.mdx'
letter: 'a'
word: 'autotroph'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'ecology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="autotroph">Autotroph</a> - Any organism that is able to manufacture its own food. Most plants are autotrophs, as are many protists and bacteria. Contrast with consumer. Autotrophs may be **Photoautotrophic**, using light energy to manufacture food, or **Chemoautotrophic**, using chemical energy.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_botany_a_axil.mdx'
letter: 'a'

dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'botany'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="axil">Axil</a> - The angle formed between a leaf stalk and the stem to which it is attached. In flowering plants, buds develop in the axils of leaves.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_b_backbone.mdx'
letter: 'b'
word: 'backbone'

<a id="backbone">Backbone</a> - Term used in [DNA cloning](#cloning_molecular_cloning) to refer to a [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) construct that serves as destination for other [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) parts.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_b_bacteria.mdx'
letter: 'b'
word: 'bacteria'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['microOrganism' ,'prokaryote' ,'unicellular' ,'nucleus' ,'gene' ,'circular_prokaryote_chromosome' ,'plasmid']
linkedFrom: ['ahl','antibiotics','antibody','codon','escherichia_coli_e_coli','lux_system_luxi_luxr','marker','petri_dish','plate_reader','prokaryote','strain','toxin','transfection','transformation','unicellular']
---

<a id="bacteria">Bacteria</a> - Bacteria are a [microorganisms](#microOrganism), classified as [prokaryotes](#prokaryote). They most often present themselves in a [unicellular](#unicellular) form and always lack a [nucleus](#nucleus). Their [genetic material](#gene) floats freely inside the cell and can be organised into two different sets, a [central circular chromosome](#circular_prokaryote_chromosome) and [plasmids](#plasmid).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_b_bacterial-colony.mdx'
letter: 'b'
word: 'bacterial-colony'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['petri_dish' ,'cell' ,'division']
linkedFrom: ['ahl','screening']
---

<a id="bacterial_colony">Bacterial Colony</a> - A colony is a point of bacteria growing on a [Petri dish](#petri_dish). If the dishes are prepared correctly then this single point of bacteria should all be issue from the same stock, *i.e.* one single [cell](#cell) was deposited onto the medium and he is the one who [divided](#division) in order to produce the others in the colony. All cells in a colony should be genetically identical.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_cellular-biology_b_bacteriophage.mdx'
letter: 'b'
word: 'bacteriophage'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'cellular-biology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="bacteriophage">Bacteriophage</a> - Virus which infects and destroys a bacterial host. Some phages, however, will incorporate their DNA into that of their host, and remain dormant for an extended period. For this reason, they have become essential tools of genetic engineers.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_b_basal.mdx'
letter: 'b'
word: 'basal'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['geneExpression']
linkedFrom: ['constitutive']
---

<a id="basal">Basal</a> - Baseline level. For example, there might be basal [gene expression](#geneExpression) in the absence of activators or in the presence of repressors. This is the minimum amount of [gene expression](#geneExpression). The basal expression level can drastically affect the performance of systems, *exempli gratia* in positive autoregulation.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="basal_group">Basal Group</a> - The earliest diverging group within a clade; for instance, to hypothesize that sponges are basal animals is to suggest that the lineage(s) leading to sponges diverged from the lineage that gave rise to all other animals.

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="biramous">Biramous</a> - Arthropod appendages that are biramous have two branches, an outer branch and an inner branch. These branches may have separate functions; in crustaceans, for instance, the inner branch of a leg is used for walking, while the outer branch may be paddle-shaped or feathery and often functions as a gill. Contrast with uniramous.

---

<a id="brain">Brain</a> - Collection of nerve cells usually located at the anterior end of an animal, when present at all. The nerves coordinate information gathered by sense organs, locomotion, and most internal body activities.

<a id="bryophyte">Bryophyte</a> - Plants in which the gametophyte generation is the larger, persistent phase; they generally lack conducting tissues. Bryophytes include the Hepaticophyta (liverworts), Anthocerotophyta (hornworts), and Bryophyta (mosses).

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_c_c-terminus-c-ter.mdx'

---

<a id="c_terminus_c_ter">C Terminus (C-ter)</a> - Also called the carboxyl-terminus or the COOH-terminus, this refers to the end of an [amino acid](#amino_acid) chain which holds the chemical group of COOH. Note this is the end of the chain which is generated last; the [N terminus](#nTerminus) is the first to come out of the [ribosome](#ribosome) during [translation](#translation).

---

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="cag_promoter_pcag">CAG Promoter (pCAG)</a> - The CAG promoter is a strong [promoter](#promoter) for expressing proteins in mammalian cells. It is composed of [Cytolomegalovirus' (CMV)](#cmv) [promoter](#promoter) enhancer region, chicken Î²-Actin promoter its first [intron](#intron) and [exon](#exon), finally the rabbit Î²-Globin splice acceptor. Hence: **C**ytomegalovirus **A**ctin **G**lobin = CAG.

<a id="crispr_cas9">CRISPR Cas9</a> - A new tool based on the bacterial CRISPR-Cas system to target and cut [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid), thus allowing for targeted [genome](#genome) editing. CRISPR stands for clustered regularly interspaced short palindromic repeats.

---

<a id="calcite">Calcite</a> - A common crystalline form of natural calcium carbonate, CaCO3, that is the basic constituent of limestone, marble, and chalk. Also called calcspar.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_c_calcium-carbonate.mdx'
letter: 'c'
word: 'calcium-carbonate'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'biochemistry'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="calcium_carbonate">Calcium Carbonate</a> - A white compound, CaCO3, that occurs naturally as marble, chalk, limestone, and calcite. It is used by many marine invertebrates, such as corals and echinoderms, and by protists, such as coccolithophorids, to construct their exoskeletons. Calcium carbonate, in the form of calcite, is also incorporated into the eggshells of amniotes, except for turtles whose eggs are composed of aragonite (CaCO3 \+ magnesium).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="canopy">Canopy</a> - Layer of vegetation elevated above the ground, usually of tree braches and epiphytes. In tropical forests, the canopy may be more than 100 feet above the ground.

---

<a id="cathodoluminescence">Cathodoluminescence</a> - An analytical technique used in geology and paleontology to analyze the different minerals in a sample, or diagenetic history of a sample â how crystals grew, were deformed, and were replaced. A beam of electrons is fired at a sample to produce visible light, which can then be used to interpret the mineralogical and diagenetic history of the sample.

---
fileName: 'biology_cellular-biology_c_cell.mdx'
letter: 'c'
word: 'cell'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'cellular-biology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['cell_membrane' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'heredity']
linkedFrom: ['apoptosis','bacterial_colony','cell_culture','facs','facs','flow_cytometry','flow_cytometry','modrna','nucleus','pathway','pathway','rna_seq','rna_seq','replicon','sachharomyces_cerevisiae','sensing','state_variable','tight_junction','transcriptome','transcriptome','transfection','unicellular','vp16','Î²_cells','Î²_cells']
---

<a id="cell">Cell</a> - The fundamental structural unit of all life. The cell consists primarily of an outer [plasma membrane](#cell_membrane), which separates it from the environment; the genetic material ([DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid)), which encodes [heritable](#heredity) information for the maintainance of life; and the cytoplasm, a heterogeneous assemblage of ions, molecules, and fluid.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

---

<a id="cell_culture">Cell Culture</a> - A cell culture is the act of growing [cells](#cell). Many different methods for doing so exist. Including [Petri dish](#petri_dish) with [LA medium](#laMedium), ([lysogeny broth](#lysogeny_broth) plus [agar](#agar)), or even pure [lysogeny broth medium](#lysogeny_broth).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_cellular-biology_c_cell-cycle.mdx'
letter: 'c'
word: 'cell-cycle'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'cellular-biology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="cell_cycle">Cell Cycle</a> - Complete sequence of steps which must be performed by a cell in order to replicate itself, as seen from mitotic event to mitotic event. Most of the cycle consists of a growth period in which the cell takes on mass and replicates its DNA. Arrest of the cell cycle is an important feature in the reproduction of many organisms, including humans.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="cell_membrane">Cell Membrane</a> - The outer membrane of a cell, which separates it from the environment. Also called a [plasma membrane](#cell_membrane).

<a id="cell_wall">Cell Wall</a> - Rigid structure deposited outside the cell membrane. Plants are known for their cell walls of cellulose, as are the green algae and certain protists, while fungi have cell walls of chitin.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_c_cellulose.mdx'

dataSource: 'berkeley'

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="cellulose">Cellulose</a> - carbohydrate polymer of the simple sugar glucose. It is found in the cell walls of plants and green algae, as well as dinoflagellates. Cellulose is the most abundant compound on earth that is manufactured by living things.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="chelicera">Chelicera</a> - The first pair of appendages of a chelicerate arthropod. Originally a short clawed appendage, the chelicerae of many arachnids are highly modified for feeding; in spiders, for instance, they are modified into poisonous fangs.

<a id="chitin">Chitin</a> - A carbohydrate polymer found in the cell walls of fungi and in the exoskeletons of arthropods, which provides strength for support and protection.

<a id="chlorophyll">Chlorophyll</a> - The green-coloured pigment that absorbs light during photosynthesis, often found in plants, algae, and some bacteria; it includes a porphyrin ring, and often has a long hydrophobic tail.

<a id="chordate">Chordate</a> - An animal with a notochord (a cartilaginous rod that extends the length of the body), dorsal hollow nerve cord (a fluid-filled tube that runs the length of the body), gill slits or pouches, and a tail at some stage in its life cycle.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_c_chromatin.mdx'

word: 'chromatin'

---

<a id="chromatin">Chromatin</a> - Is a method of organising and highly compacting [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). It is formed from a [complex](#complex) of various [molecules](#molecule) including [proteins](#protein), [RNA](#rna), and of course [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). Chromatin can be organised into two different forms; one which composes the other. [Euchromatin](#euchromatin) and [heterochromatin](#heteroChromatin) respectively.

---

<a id="clade">Clade</a> - A monophyletic taxon; a group of organisms which includes the most recent common ancestor of all of its members and all of the descendants of that most recent common ancestor. From the Greek word "klados", meaning branch or twig.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="cladogenesis">Cladogenesis</a> - The development of a new clade; the splitting of a single lineage into two distinct lineages; speciation.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_phylogenetics_c_cladogram.mdx'
letter: 'c'
word: 'cladogram'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'phylogenetics'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="cladogram">Cladogram</a> - A diagram, resulting from a cladistic analysis, which depicts a hypothetical branching sequence of lineages leading to the taxa under consideration. The points of branching within a cladogram are called nodes. All taxa occur at the endpoints of the cladogram.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="cloning_molecular_cloning">Cloning (Molecular Cloning)</a> - The assembly and replication of new [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) constructs from existing pieces of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid).

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_c_codon.mdx'
letter: 'c'
word: 'codon'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['ribonucleotides' ,'mrna' ,'amino_acid' ,'microOrganism' ,'bacteria' ,'trna' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid']
linkedFrom: ['anticodon','mrna','protein','rna_polymerase_rna_p','ribosome_binding_site_rbs','trna']
---

<a id="codon">Codon</a> - A triplet (three) of [ribonucleotides](#ribonucleotides) in [mRNA](#mrna) that encodes for an [amino acid](#amino_acid).

 Note that whether or not a codon matches this table depends on the organism. Some organisms, especially [microorganisms](#microOrganism) and [bacteria](#bacteria) often present modified readings of these codons (known as alternative codons). This is dependant on the presence or not of a [tRNA](#trna) capable of matching the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) sequence (codon).

| Common Start/Stop Codons |     |          |            |              |
| ------------------------ | --- | -------- | ---------- | ------------ |
| RNA                      | DNA | Function | Amino Acid | Organisms    |
| AUG                      | ATG | Start    | Methionine | General      |
| CUG                      | CTG | Start    | Leucine    | Mammals Rare |
| AUA                      | ATA | Start    | Methionine | Mitochondria |
| AUU                      | ATT | Start    | Methionine |              |
| GUG                      | GTG | Start    | Methionine | Prokaryotes  |
| UUG                      | TTG | Start    | Methionine |              |
| UAA                      | TAA | Stop     | Ochre      | Universal    |
| UAG                      | TAG | Stop     | Amber      |              |
| UGA                      | TGA | Stop     | Opal       |              |

<a id="coelom">Coelom</a> - Fluid-filled cavity within the body of an animal; usually refers to a cavity lined with specialised tissue peritoneum in which the gut is suspended. The structure and development of the coelom is an important character for recognizing major groups of animals.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

linksTo: ['']

---

<a id="coenocytic">Coenocytic</a> - Condition in which an organism consists of filamentous cells with large central vacuoles, and whose nuclei are not partitioned into separate compartments. The result is a long tube containing many nuclei, with all the cytoplasm at the periphery.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="collagen">Collagen</a> - long proteins whose structure is wound into a triple helix. The resulting fibers have a high tensile strength. Collagen is a primary component of mammalian hair.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="colonial">Colonial</a> - Condition in which many unicellular organisms live together in a somewhat coordinated group. Unlike true multicellular organisms, the individual cells retain their separate identities, and usually, their own membranes and cell walls.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="columella">Columella</a> - A small column of tissue which runs up through the center of a spore capsule. It is present in hornworts, mosses, and some rhyniophytes.

<a id="complementary">Complementary</a> - Complementary is refering the physical matching of two corresponding parts, this may be seen simply as two puzzle pieces fitting together. This term is often used when refering to genetic material and more specifically a pair of strands composed of either [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid)/[DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) or [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid)/[RNA](#rna) or [RNA](#rna)/[RNA](#rna), and even [proteins](#protein) with [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) or [RNA](#rna).

<a id="compound_eye">Compound Eye</a> - Found in many but not all arthropods, a compound eye is composed of a large number of small, closely packed simple eyes (ommatidia), each with its own lens and nerve receptors.

<a id="context">Context</a> - The setting in which something occurs. Context is important in chemical or biochemistryical reactions, as some proteins or chemicals will not act or demonstrate normal activity relative to their chemical environments. This is often the case with proteins which will [denature](#denature) in the wrong pH.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="contractile_vacuole">Contractile Vacuole</a> - In many protists, a specialised vacuole with associated channels designed to collect excess water in the cell. Microtubules periodically contract to force this excess water out of the cell, regulating the cell's osmotic balance.

<a id="convergence">Convergence</a> - Similarities which have arisen independently in two or more organisms that are not closely related. Contrast with homology.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_c_cooperativity.mdx'
letter: 'c'
word: 'cooperativity'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['promoter' ,'CDic_oxygen' ,'hemoglobin' ,'molecule' ,'repressor' ,'MDic_exponential']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="cooperativity">Cooperativity</a> - The ability for binding events to [promote](#promoter) additional binding events. *Exempli gratia* the binding of the first [oxygen molecule](#CDic_oxygen) to [hemoglobin](#hemoglobin) makes the binding of the second [oxygen molecule](#CDic_oxygen) much more likely, which in turn makes the binding of the third [molecule](#molecule) much more likely, *et cetera*. We often want to use [repressors](#repressor) that exhibit cooperativity, as they exhibit a non-linear ([exponential](#MDic_exponential)) response useful for creating devices that can be analysed with the digital abstraction.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_botany_c_cotyledon.mdx'

dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="cotyledon">Cotyledon</a> - The "seed leaves" produced by the embryo of a seed plant that serve to absorb nutrients packaged in the seed, until the seedling is able to produce its first true leaves and begin photosynthesis; the number of cotyledons is a key feature for the identification of the two major groups of flowering plants.

<a id="cuticle">Cuticle</a> - In animals, a multilayered, extracellular, external body covering, usually composed of fibrous molecules such as chitin or collagen, and sometimes strengthened by the deposition of minerals such as calcium carbonate. A waxy layer which seals the outer surface of land plants, helping to retain moisture.

<a id="cytoskeleton">Cytoskeleton</a> - Integrated system of molecules within eukaryotic cells which provides them with shape, internal spatial organization, motility, and may assist in communication with other cells and the environment. Red blood cells, for instance, would be spherical instead of flat if it were not for their cytoskeleton.

linkedFrom: d_3','5_prime_end_5','5_prime_end_5']

<a id="dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid">DNA (Desoxyribonucleic Acid)</a> - A [molecule](#molecule) ([nucleic acid](#nucleic_acid)) which carries most of the genetic instructions used in the development, function and reproduction of all known living organisms and many [viruses](#virus). DNA is the primary compenent of [chromosomes](#chromosome).

DNA a double helix molecule, the current known basis for life.

 DNA is composed of two directional strands. The directionality of these strands is dictated by the orientation of the [nucleotides](#nucleotide) that compose it; there is a [5' end](#5_prime_end_5) and a [3' end](#5_prime_end_5).

 Four different [nucleotides](#nucleotide) compose DNA, these are differentiated by the nucleic bases they hold: [adenine (A)](#adenine), [thymine (T)](#thymine), [guanine (G)](#guanine), and [cytosine (C)](#cytosine). These can grouped together chemically into the purine group A, T, and the pyrimidine group G, C. The two strands come together and bind through weak [hydrogen bonds](#hydrogenBond); A - T (2 bonds), and C - G (3 bonds).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="de_novo">*De Novo*</a> - From scratch. *exempli gratia:* *de novo* [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) synthesis is the synthesis of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) from basic building blocks such as [nucleotides](#nucleotide) or [oligonucleotides](#oligonucleotide), instead of creating a new [DNA molecule](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) that is a copy of an existing [DNA molecule](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid); that would be templated synthesis.

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_d_degenerated-primer-library.mdx'
letter: 'd'
word: 'degenerated-primer-library'
dictionary: 'biology'

linksTo: ['selex_systematic_evolution_of_ligands_by_exponential_enrichment']

---

<a id="degenerated_primer_library">Degenerated Primer Library</a> - A degenerate primer library is a mix of primers used in [SELEX](#selex_systematic_evolution_of_ligands_by_exponential_enrichment). These primers are obtained by chemical synthesis; note that in chemistry DNA sequences are generated in the reverse sense, 3' â 5'. These primers should contain common regions and "degenerated regions". These degenerated regions are denoted as N; N meaning any of the 4 nucleotides may occupy that spot. Note that if a sequence is ordered with 40N then that would mean that there are 440 \= 1.2 Â· 1024 different sequences possible. Note the tube received will contain a mixture of all the different possible sequences and not just specific ones.

 Reminder for mol, M, definition see Concentration, Matter, & Volumes


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---
fileName: 'biology_phylogenetics_d_derived.mdx'
letter: 'd'
word: 'derived'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'phylogenetics'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="derived">Derived</a> - Describes a character state that is present in one or more subclades, but not all, of a clade under consideration. A derived character state is inferred to be a modified version of the primitive condition of that character, and to have arisen later in the evolution of the clade. For example, "presence of hair" is a primitive character state for all mammals, whereas the "hairlessness" of whales is a derived state for one subclade within the Mammalia.

In humans dextrose does not need to be [metabolised](#metabolism) and can be integrated and used directly in its current form by human cells.

---
fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_d_double-inverse-lineweaver-burk-plot-double-reciprocal-plot.mdx'
letter: 'd'
word: 'double-inverse-lineweaver-burk-plot-double-reciprocal-plot'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'biochemistry'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['michaelis_menten_kinetics' ,'inhibition']
linkedFrom: ['inhibition','michaelis_menten_kinetics']
---

<a id="double_inverse_lineweaver_burk_plot_double_reciprocal_plot">Double inverse/Lineweaver-Burk plot/double reciprocal plot</a> - A graphical reprsentation of the Lineweaver-Burk equation used in enzyme cinetics. The plot allows us to derive useful information as to the nature of a [Michaelis-Menten](#michaelis_menten_kinetics) type reaction. The reciprocal of the formula is the following:

 $$ V = \frac{V_{max}\[S\]}{K_m + \[S\]} $$ $$ \frac{1}{V} = \frac{K_m + \[S\]}{V_{max}\[S\]} = \frac{K_m}{V_{max}} \cdot \frac{1}{\[S\]} + \frac{1}{V_{max}} $$

An example of the double inverse plot. Multiple points must be calculated from the resulting formula. The condition that varies is concetration of the substrate experimentally: 1/\[s\].

 Note that this equation's simplified form comes out to the form Y = Ax + B. This can be described as a linear curve on a graph as shown.

 This method can be used to determine enzyme cinetics: Km, Vmax. The y-intercept of the graph is equivalent to the inverse of Vmax, and the x-intercept represents -1/KVm.

Enzyme inhibition shown using the double inverse. The different motifs formed by the curves allows us to deduce the type of inhibiton.

 These representations also allow us to visualise the different forms of [enzyme inhibition](#inhibition).

 See also: [Michaelis-Menten Kinetics](#michaelis_menten_kinetics), and [Enzyme inhibition](#inhibition).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_e_electrophoresis.mdx'
letter: 'e'
word: 'electrophoresis'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'protein' ,'rna' ,'northernBlot' ,'southern_blot' ,'western_blot_immunoblot' ,'2d_electrophoresis' ,'capillaryElectrophoresis' ,'pulsed_field_electrophoresis']
linkedFrom: ['agar','agarose','southern_blot','western_blot_immunoblot','2d_electrophoresis','2d_electrophoresis']
---

<a id="electrophoresis">Electrophoresis</a> - From electr(ic) and phoresis the action of carrying. The separation of ions (charged particules) by use of an electrical field. This allows for separation according to differences in mobility which is dependent on the charge/mass ratio. This technique is commonly used to separate pieces of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) or [proteins](#protein) by size, shape, and charge. This technique can also be used for [RNA](#rna).
- Variants of this technique are the following:
- [Northern Blot](#northernBlot)
- [Southern Blot](#southern_blot)
- [Western Blot](#western_blot_immunoblot)
- [Two Dimensional Gel Electrophoresis (2D Gel)](#2d_electrophoresis)
- [Capillary Electrophoresis](#capillaryElectrophoresis)
- [Pulsed-Field Gel Electrophoresis](#pulsed_field_electrophoresis)

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_e_enveloped-virus.mdx'

<a id="enveloped_virus">Enveloped Virus</a> - A [virus](#virus) that has an outer wrapping known as an envelope. These [viruses](#virus) are wrapped in what was before the [host](#host)'s [plasma membrane](#lipidBilayer) which is obtained in a process known as budding-off. Typically enveloped viruses are much weaker when exposed to the environment and need a host to survive. They do not survive on sterile surfaces.

---

<a id="epithelium">Epithelium</a> - Layer of cells which lines a body cavity; cells may be ciliated or unciliated, and may be squamous (flat, scale-shaped), cuboidal (cube-shaped), or columnar (column-shaped). Your stomach and cheeks are lined with epithelium.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="epitope_antigenic_determinant">Epitope (Antigenic Determinant)</a> - Part of the structre of antigens, it is the smallest possible three dimensional structure to which an [antibody](#antibody) can affix itself on said [antigens](#antigen).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_e_escherichia-coli-e-coli.mdx'
letter: 'e'
word: 'escherichia-coli-e-coli'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['bacteria' ,'strain' ,'e_coli_escherichia_coli_k12_strain' ,'pathogenic' ,'base_pair_bp' ,'transformation' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid']
linkedFrom: ['arac','ccdb','strain']
---

<a id="escherichia_coli_e_coli">*Escherichia coli (E. coli)*</a> - A family of [bacteria](#bacteria). Certain [strains](#strain) of *E. coli* are favoured by scientist in labs, most often the [*K12 strain*](#e_coli_escherichia_coli_k12_strain). Some [strains](#strain) of *E. coli,* can be [pathogenic](#pathogenic) to humans. They have a small, \~4.6 [megabasepair](#base_pair_bp) circular genome, are easily [transformed](#transformation), and replicate fast. Cell replication can be made to be limited by controlling [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) replication through predetermined growth conditions.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="esophagus">Esophagus</a> - That portion of the gut which connects the pharynx to the stomach.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_e_euchromatin.mdx'
letter: 'e'
word: 'euchromatin'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

---

<a id="euchromatin">Euchromatin</a> - Euchromatin is a form of [chromatin](#chromatin) which is most often most present in active and [transcriptionally](#transcription) competent cells. [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) is wrapped around [histone](#histone) proteins to form what are known as nucleosomes. This DNA/protein structure resembles beads on a string.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_e_eukaryota.mdx'
letter: 'e'
word: 'eukaryota'

category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['organelle' ,'nucleus']
linkedFrom: ['activator','nucleus','petri_dish','rna_interference_rnai','rna_polymerase_rna_p','replicon','ribosome_binding_site_rbs','sachharomyces_cerevisiae','vp16','yeast','yeast']
---

<a id="eukaryota">Eukaryota</a> - Organisms with membrane-bound [organelles](#organelle), and cytoskeletons. These organisms posses a [nucleus](#nucleus) which contains their genetic material, and is enclosed by the [nuclear envelope](#nucleus). Protists, plants, animals, and fungi, all fall into this domain of life.

<a id="eustele">Eustele</a> - When a plant's vascular tissue develops in discrete bundles, it is said to have a eustele. See also protostele and siphonostele.

<a id="evolution">Evolution</a> - Darwin's definition: descent with modification. The term has been variously used and abused since Darwin to include everything from the origin of man to the origin of life.

<a id="evolutionary_tree">Evolutionary Tree</a> - A diagram which depicts the hypothetical phylogeny of the taxa under consideration. The points at which lineages split represent ancestor taxa to the descendant taxa appearing at the terminal points of the cladogram.

<a id="expression">Expression</a> - Expression refers the creation of something. In a biological context by convention it refers to the creation of a protein from a gene. Gene expression thus refers to the amount of a protein being produced from the gene in question.

---
fileName: 'biology_cellular-biology_e_extracellular-matrix.mdx'

dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="extracellular_matrix">Extracellular Matrix</a> - (ECM) Region outside of metazoan cells which includes compounds attached to the plasma membrane, as well as dissolved substances attracted to the surface charge of the cells. The ECM functions both to keep animal cells adhered together, and well as buffering them from their environment.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="eyespot">Eyespot</a> - Light-sensitive organelle found in many groups of protists, and in some metazoans.

<a id="facs">FACS</a> - A type offlow cytometry for sorting a mixture of [cells](#cell) into two or more containers, one [cell](#cell) at a time, based upon the [fluorescent](#fluorescence) characteristics of each cell. Cells can be manipulated to express [fluorescent](#fluorescence) properties in order to sort them by FACS.

<a id="fission">Fission</a> - Division of single-celled organisms, especially prokaryotes, in which mitosis does not occur. Also used to refer to mitosis in certain unicellular fungi.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

---

<a id="flagellin">Flagellin</a> - protein which is the primary component of prokaryotic flagella.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_cellular-biology_f_flagellum.mdx'
letter: 'f'
word: 'flagellum'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'cellular-biology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="flagellum">Flagellum</a> - Hair-like structure attached to a cell, used for locomotion in many protists and prokaryotes. The prokaryotic flagellum differs from the eukaryotic flagellum in that the prokaryotic flagellum is a solid unit composed primarily of the protein flagellin, while the eukaryotic flagellum is composed of several protein strands bound by a membrane, and does not contain flagellin. The eukaryotic flagellum is sometimes referred to as an undulipodium.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="flow_cytometry">Flow Cytometry</a> - A laser based technology employed for counting [cells](#cell), [cell](#cell) sorting, and [biomarker](#biomarker) detection. It works by suspending cells in a stream of fluid and passing them by an electronic detection apparatus.

<a id="food_chain">Food Chain</a> - All the interactions of predator and prey, included along with the exchange of nutrients into and out of the soil. These interactions connect the various members of an ecosystem, and describe how energy passes from one organism to another.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_g_gibbs-free-energy.mdx'
letter: 'g'
word: 'gibbs-free-energy'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['enthalpy' ,'exothermic' ,'heat' ,'system' ,'endothermic']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="gibbs_free_energy">Gibbs Free Energy</a> - A state function discovered by Josiah Willard Gibbs called Gibbs Free Energy, Free [Enthalpy](#enthalpy), or G. This function is written at a given temperature as such: $$ \Delta G = \Delta H - T \Delta S $$.

[Exothermic](#exothermic) reactions are instances where [heat](#heat) is liberated from the [system](#system); in this case [enthalpy](#enthalpy) is negative (Î\<H). These systems are inherently unstable and thus spontaneous reactions.

[Endothermic](#endothermic) reactions are instances where [heat](#heat) is absorbed by the [system](#system); in this case [enthalpy](#enthalpy) is positve (Î\>H).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_g_gibson-assembly.mdx'
letter: 'g'
word: 'gibson-assembly'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['cloning_molecular_cloning' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="gibson_assembly">Gibson Assembly</a> - [DNA cloning](#cloning_molecular_cloning) method which allows for the joining of multiple [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) fragments in a single, isothermal reaction.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_g_gill.mdx'

word: 'gill'

category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="gill">Gill</a> - In aquatic animals, highly vascularized tissues with large surface area; these are extended out of the body and into the surrounding water for gas exchange.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_g_gill-arches.mdx'
letter: 'g'
word: 'gill-arches'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="gill_arches">Gill Arches</a> - Stiffenings which support the flesh between the gill slits of chordates. In most vertebrates, the first gill arches have been modified to form the jaw, and in tetrapods, the inner ear bones.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_g_gill-slit.mdx'
letter: 'g'
word: 'gill-slit'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="gill_slit">Gill Slit</a> - A slitlike or porelike opening connecting the pharynx of a chordate with the outside of the body. Gill slits may contain the gills and be used for gas exchange, as in most fish, but may also be used for filter-feeding, or may be highly modified in land-dwelling vertebrates.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_g_glucose.mdx'
letter: 'g'
word: 'glucose'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'biochemistry'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['lacz']
---

<a id="glucose">Glucose</a> - simple sugar, and the primary product of photosynthesis. It is polymerized to make cellulose and chitin.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_g_glycoprotein.mdx'
letter: 'g'
word: 'glycoprotein'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'biochemistry'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="glycoprotein">Glycoprotein</a> - A membrane-bound protein which has attached branching carbohydrates. These may function in cell-cell recognition, such as in human blood groups and immune system response, as well as in resisting compression of cells.

<a id="golden_gate">Golden Gate</a> - A [DNA cloning](#cloning_molecular_cloning) method to simultaneously assemble multiple [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) fragments into a single piece using Type IIs [restriction enzymes](#restriction_enzyme) and T4 DNA [ligase](#ligase_ligation).

<a id="golgi_apparatus">Golgi Apparatus</a> - Eukaryotic organelle which package cell products, such as enzymes and hormones, and coordinate their transport to the outside of the cell.

---

<a id="gradualism">Gradualism</a> - A model of evolution that assumes slow, steady rates of change. Charles Darwin's original concept of evolution by natural selection assumed gradualism. Contrast with punctuated equilibrium.

---
fileName: 'biology_ecology_g_grassland.mdx'

word: 'grassland'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'ecology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="grassland">Grassland</a> - Region in which the climate is dry for long periods of the summer, and freezes in the winter. Grasslands are characterized by grasses and other erect herbs, usually without trees or shrubs. Grasslands occur in the dry temperate interiors of continents, and first appeared in the Miocene.

<a id="groundwater">Groundwater</a> - Water found underground as a result of rainfall, ice and snow melt, submerged rivers, lakes, and springs. This water often carries minerals. These minerals can accumulate in the remains of buried organisms and eventually cause fossilization.

<a id="hemoglobin">Hemoglobin</a> - An [iron](#CDic_iron) containing [metalloprotein](#metalloProtein) complex which is essential for bonding, transporting, and distributing oxygen throughout the body. This protein complex circulates in the blood of most chordates and the roots of certain legumes; in chordates this is the means by which oxygen is delivered to the cells.

<a id="heterochromatin">Heterochromatin</a> - [Euchromatin](#euchromatin) is wrapped into 30nm strcutures to form the megastructure known as heterochromatin. Heterochromatin is most often present in cells which are inactive, [senescent](#senescent), or otherwise dormant. This 30nm string composes the active [chromosome](#chromosome) during [interphase](#interphase).

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_i_immunogenicity.mdx'
letter: 'i'
word: 'immunogenicity'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['antigen' ,'molecule' ,'epitope_antigenic_determinant' ,'antibody' ,'complementary' ,'paratope_antigen_binding_site']
linkedFrom: ['antigenicity']
---

<a id="immunogenicity">Immunogenicity</a> - Is the potential of a substance to induce an immune response. This depends on various factors:
- The species and state of the animal - its genome, immunological past, and physiological state.
- The degree of structural similarity of the [antigen](#antigen) to the [molecules](#molecule) of the target animal.
- The dose of the injected [antigen](#antigen).
- The physical and chemical characteristics of the [antigen](#antigen):  
   - Its size it must contain at least two [epitopes](#epitope_antigenic_determinant) in order to be fixed by an [antibody](#antibody).  
   - Its form if it is a particle or not.  
   - Its rigidity in order to be [complementary](#complementary) to other [paratopes](#paratope_antigen_binding_site).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_i_in-vitro.mdx'
letter: 'i'
word: 'in-vitro'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="in_vitro">*In vitro*</a> - Used to refer to experiments conducted outside of a living animal. *Exempli gratia* cell cultures are often used in artificial containers to conduct experiments in controlled conditions on living cells.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_i_in-vivo.mdx'
letter: 'i'
word: 'in-vivo'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="in_vivo">*In vivo*</a> - Used to refer to experiments conducted in a living animal. *Exempli gratia* mice are often used in labs to experiment on living organisms as they represent a well known and well defined mammalian analog.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_i_incubation.mdx'
letter: 'i'
word: 'incubation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="incubation">Incubation</a> - In birds and reptiles, the maintaining of a constant temperature during the development of the embryo. Birds incubate their eggs by sitting on them (also called brooding),while other animals, like crocodiles, bury their eggs in organic matter. If eggs are not incubated, the embryos within those eggs generally die. Some dinosaurs may have incubated their eggs by burial in sediment, in organic matter, or by brooding like birds.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_i_induction.mdx'

word: 'induction'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['molecule']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="induction">Induction</a> - A system that can be induced by another [molecule](#molecule), called an inducer, is an inducible system. Induction is the process of activating a system.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="ingroup">Ingroup</a> - In a cladistic analysis, the set of taxa which are hypothesized to be more closely related to each other than any are to the outgroup.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_i_inhibition.mdx'
letter: 'i'
word: 'inhibition'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['molecule' ,'double_inverse_lineweaver_burk_plot_double_reciprocal_plot']
linkedFrom: ['double_inverse_lineweaver_burk_plot_double_reciprocal_plot']
---

<a id="inhibition">Inhibition</a> - A [molecule](#molecule) that can cause the arrest or tamper the activity of a reaction is called an inhibitor. In the context of biology an inhibitor has a negative effect on a reaction catalysed by an enzyme. There are multiple cases into which an inhibition may be classed:

Types of inhibition, the concentration of of the inhibitor is the only thing that changes.

- Competitive inhibition: Km increased, Vmax unaffected. The inhibitor matches the active site and fixes itself there.
- Un-competitive inhibition: Km reduced, Vmax reduced. The inhibitor matches a zone close to the active site and thus impedes the substrate from fixing itself there.
- Non-competitive: Km unaffected, Vmax reduced. The inhibtor fixes itself somewhere else on the enzyme and changes the conformation of the active site.

 See also: [Double inverse](#double_inverse_lineweaver_burk_plot_double_reciprocal_plot).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---
fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_i_isotopic-analysis.mdx'
letter: 'i'
word: 'isotopic-analysis'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'biochemistry'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="isotopic_analysis">Isotopic Analysis</a> - The study of the geochemistry of stable isotopes in naturally occurring sediments and biological structures. Stable isotopes are atomic variations of elements that are stable over long periods of time, meaning they do not radioactively decay. Several elements, like oxygen and carbon, have several stable forms. Oxygen, for example, occurs in nature as 16O and 18O â these two forms are isotopes. They have different numbers of neutrons (16O has two more neutrons than 18O), and and is therefore heavier. Because the two isotopes have different masses, chemical and physical reactions like bonding, evaporation, and precipitation occur at different frequencies. The ratio of stable isotopes is preserved in chemical compounds like water, ice, and calcium carbonate and provides information on the environmental conditions at the time the compound formed. For example, the ratio of 18O/16O in an ice sample is linked to the water temperature of ancient oceans, which in turn reflects ancient climates.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="kinase">Kinase</a> - An [enzyme](#enzyme) that adds a [phosphate group](#phosphateGroup) to some chemical moiety. For [enzymes](#enzyme), the resulting change in [phosphorylation](#phosphorylation) state can change the activity of the [enzyme](#enzyme) (reduce or increase it, change the substrate [affinity](#affinity), or change the reaction being [catalysed](#catalysation)). For [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid), a phosphate on the [5'](#5_prime_end_5) end of a piece of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) is required for it to be ligated to another piece of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid).

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_l_ligase-ligation.mdx'
letter: 'l'
word: 'ligase-ligation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['enzyme' ,'catalysation' ,'molecule' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'rna' ,'polymer' ,'doubleStrand' ,'substrate' ,'oligonucleotide' ,'pnk']
linkedFrom: ['golden_gate','ligation']
---

<a id="ligase_ligation">Ligase, Ligation</a> - A ligase is an [enzyme](#enzyme) that [catalyses](#catalysation) the formation of a covalent bond between large [molecules](#molecule), *exempli gratia* [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) or [RNA](#rna), for which it catalyses the formation of the phosphodiester bond in the backbone of the nucleic acid [polymer](#polymer) Ligases can use single-stranded or [double-stranded](#doubleStrand) (more common) [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) (or even [RNA](#rna)) as the [substrate](#substrate) but are often [substrate](#substrate) to the type of [substrate](#substrate), while not being sequence-specific. All commonly used ligases require a **5'** phosphate group on the [substrate](#substrate), which is absent from most synthetic [oligonucleotides](#oligonucleotide) and thus have to be specifically ordered as such or enzymatically phosphorylated with a [poly-nucleotide kinase (PNK)](#pnk).

<a id="ligation">Ligation</a> - The act of joining to separate objects or components together. See [ligase](#ligase_ligation) for information on the joining of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid).

<a id="mtoc">MTOC</a> - (microtubule organizing center) MTOCs are bundles of protein tubes which may be found at the base of a eukaryotic flagellum. In animals, they also function in creating the arrays of microtubules that pull the chromosomes apart during mitosis.

<a id="marker">Marker</a> - In the context of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) assembly, a [gene](#gene) that enables the screening or selection of [bacteria](#bacteria) containing our desired marker. This could be a [gene](#gene) that is toxic to the cell (negative selection; *exempli gratia* [ccdB](#ccdb)), a [gene](#gene) that confers antibiotic resistance (positive selection; *exempli gratia* [KanR](#kanamycinResistance)), or a [gene](#gene) that turns the bacterial colonies some colour (*exempli gratia* [LacZ](#lacz), or a [fluorescent](#fluorescence) protein such as [RFP](#rfp)).

<a id="mass_action_kinetics">Mass-Action Kinetics</a> - A method of modelling chemical reaction rates. In this kinetic scheme, the rate of a reaction is proportional to the product of the [concentrations](#concentration) of reacting species.

<a id="master_equation">Master Equation</a> - A form of chemical kinetic equation that describes the time evolution of all possible states of a chemical system. Master equations are commonly used in stochastic simulations in conjunction with the Gillespie algorithm simulations.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_m_melting-temperature.mdx'
letter: 'm'
word: 'melting-temperature'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="melting_temperature">Melting Temperature</a> - Melting temperature is referring the the dehybridisation temperature of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) primers (most often). For calculating these temperatures, which are to be used when designating a [PCR](#polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr) protocol, the following formulas are to be used:

 For primers with a length inferiour to 14 nt the following is used:

 $$ Tm = (n(A) + n(T)) \cdot 2 + (n(G) + n(C)) \cdot 4 $$

 For primers with a length superiour to 13 nt the following is used:

 $$ Tm = 64.9 + 41 \cdot \frac{(n(G) + n(C) - 16.4)}{(n(A) + n(T) + n(G) + n(C))} $$

 Both these formulas assume the following: 50 nM primer, 50 mM Na+, and pH 7.0\. n(x) designates the number of whichever base.

<a id="mesoderm">Mesoderm</a> - In animals with three tissue layers (i.e. all except sponges and cnidarians), the middle layer of tissue, between the ectoderm and the endoderm. In vertebrates, for instance, the mesoderm forms the skeleton, muscles, heart, spleen, and many other internal organs.

<a id="metabolism">Metabolism</a> - The chemical processes within an organic body that supply the energy necessary for life. The rate of metabolic processes is sometimes used as a way to differentiate organisms. For example, mammals generally have a higher metabolism than reptiles and can thus sustain higher levels of activity for longer periods of time.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_m_michaelis-menten-kinetics.mdx'
letter: 'm'
word: 'michaelis-menten-kinetics'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['enzyme' ,'catalysation' ,'mass_action_kinetics' ,'concentration' ,'michaelis_menten_kinetics' ,'inhibitor' ,'double_inverse_lineweaver_burk_plot_double_reciprocal_plot']
linkedFrom: ['double_inverse_lineweaver_burk_plot_double_reciprocal_plot','michaelis_menten_kinetics']
---

<a id="michaelis_menten_kinetics">Michaelis-Menten Kinetics</a> - A chemical kinetic scheme for describing the rate of an [enzyme](#enzyme)\-[catalysed](#catalysation) processes. It relates the rate of reaction rate V at which the product \[P\] is formed, to the depletion of the substrate \[S\] from which it is produced. These are linked by Km the Michaelis constant, which corresponds to the substrate \[S\] concentration at which the speed v is half the vmax.

 There are a few terms to take into consideration before attacking the formula#miRna: vmax is the maximal speed at which the reaction will take place, (vmax/2) is half maximal speed, which brings us to km or the substrate concentration at which the rate of reaction will half speed.

A curve demonstrating a generique enzyme substrate reaction. The graph shows, a reaction rate/speed (concentration/s), in relation to a substrate concentration.

 $$ \nu = \frac{d\[P\]}{dt} = \frac{V_{max} \[S\]}{K_m + \[S\]} $$

 km can be isolated in the following way:

 $$ km = \frac{V_{max}\[S\] - \nu\[S\]}{\nu} $$

 Its simplest formulation considers three processes:

1. The binding of substrate to enzyme
2. The unbinding of the substrate-enzyme complex
3. The conversion of the enzyme-substrate complex to the product and the enzyme

 Using [mass-action kinetics](#mass_action_kinetics) and the assumption that [enzyme](#enzyme) [concentrations](#concentration) are much smaller than substrate [concentrations](#concentration), we get an equation for the rate of product (P) production (initial velocity); where Vmax is the maximal velocity (saturating substrate conditions) and Km is the Michaelis constant (the substrate [concentration](#concentration) at half-maximal velocity). More complex [Michaelis-Menten](#michaelis_menten_kinetics) formulations must be used if the release of the product from the enzyme-product complex is slow, ordered-binding is required, or [inhibitors](#inhibitor) are present.

 See also: [Double inverse](#double_inverse_lineweaver_burk_plot_double_reciprocal_plot) 


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="mirna">miRNA</a> - A micro [RNA](#rna) is a functional [RNA](#rna) that can [inhibit](#inhibitor) the expression of a [gene](#gene) by either [inhibiting](#inhibitor) [translation](#translation) through mostly unknown mechanisms, or destabilising the [mRNA](#mrna) through the use of [enzymes](#enzyme) in the [RNA interference (RNAi)](#rna_interference_rnai) pathway. Not all organisms have the [RNAi](#rna_interference_rnai) pathway. Notable exclusions are all [prokaryotes](#prokaryote) and [baker's yeast, *S. cerevisiae*](#sachharomyces_cerevisiae).

<a id="modrna">modRNA</a> - Modified [mRNA](#mrna). Synthetic, chemically-modified [mRNA](#mrna) that can be transfected into [cells](#cell) to induce expression of a [protein](#protein) of interest. Chemical modifications at the [5'](#5_prime_end_5) end allow the [transcript](#transcription) to evade harmful immune responses and prevent it from being degraded thus allowing prolonged protein expression.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_m_mrna.mdx'
letter: 'm'
word: 'mrna'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['rna' ,'codon' ,'translation' ,'ribosome' ,'protein' ,'intron' ,'poly_a_tail' ,'5PrimeCap' ,'PolyATail' ,'3_prime_end_3' ,'5_prime_end_5']
linkedFrom: ['antisense_sequence','codon','crick_strand','initiation','mirna','modrna','poly_cistronic','protein','rna','rna_binding_protein_rna_bp','rna_polymerase_rna_p','rna_seq','ribosome','riboswitch','transcription','translation','translational_fusion','trna','trna','untranslated_region_utr','watson_strand_5_3']
---

<a id="mrna">mRNA</a> - Messenger RNA is a functional [RNA](#rna) comprising [codons](#codon) to be [translated](#translation) by [ribosomes](#ribosome) to [proteins](#protein). In eukaryotic systems, mRNA that has not been processed is referred to as precursor mRNA (pre-mRNA). This pre-mRNA is typically processed through the removal of [introns](#intron), the addition of a [polyA tail](#poly_a_tail), and the addition of a [5' cap](#5PrimeCap) to create mature mRNA. Matured mRNA is what is translated by [ribosomes](#ribosome).
1. Mature Messenger RNA or mRNA has undergone the following steps.
2. [Introns](#intron) have been removed.
3. A [PolyA tail](#PolyATail) has been added to the [3'](#3_prime_end_3) end.
4. A [5' cap](#5PrimeCap) has been added to the [5'](#5_prime_end_5) end.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="mitochondrion">Mitochondrion</a> - Complex organelle found in most eukaryotes; believed to be descended from free-living bacteria that established a symbiotic relationship with a primitive eukaryote. Mitochondria are the site of most of the energy production in most eukaryotes; they require oxygen to function. See: double membrane.

<a id="moclo">MoClo</a> - Modular cloning (MoClo) a hierarchical [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) assembly method built on [Golden Gate](#golden_gate) technology. The use of a parts with standardised cloning sequences creates MoClo modularity. This modularity permits the automated construction of many MoClo constructs.

<a id="monomer">Monomer</a> - The basic unit of a [polymer](#polymer); monomers compose up polymers. A [nucleotide](#nucleotide) is the [monomer](#monomer) of a strand of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid), which is a [polymer](#polymer) of [desoxyribonucleic acids](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_phylogenetics_m_monophyletic.mdx'
letter: 'm'

dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'phylogenetics'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="monophyletic">Monophyletic</a> - Term applied to a group of organisms which includes the most recent common ancestor of all of its members and all of the descendants of that most recent common ancestor. A monophyletic group is called a clade.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_m_monotreme.mdx'
letter: 'm'
word: 'monotreme'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="monotreme">Monotreme</a> - A mammal that lays eggs rather than giving live birth. Though laying eggs is a primitive reptilian trait, monotremes share many morphological, physiological, and reproductive characteristics with other mammals, making them true mammals. Extant monotremes include the duck-billed platypus and echidna.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="monsoonal">Monsoonal</a> - Describes a climate pattern with a wind system that changes direction with the seasons; this pattern is dominant over the Arabian Sea and Southeast Asia.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_m_motif.mdx'
letter: 'm'
word: 'motif'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['autoregulation' ,'ffl' ,'nucleotide' ,'transcription_factor_tf' ,'amino_acid' ,'protein' ,'alpha_helix']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="motif">Motif</a> - A commonly-reproduced pattern that has a similiar function across multiple systems. Examples of regulatory network motifs are negative [autoregulation](#autoregulation) and [feed-forward loops](#ffl). [Nucleotide](#nucleotide) sequence motifs are commonly-found sequences of nucleotides that may serve as [transcription factor](#transcription_factor_tf) binding sites. [Amino acid](#amino_acid) sequence motifs may reproduce common [protein](#protein) structures such as [alpha helices](#alpha_helix).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="mouth">Mouth</a> - Front opening of the digestive tract, into which food is taken for digestion. In flatworms, the mouth is the only opening into the digestive cavity, and is located on the "belly" of the worm.

<a id="multiple_cloning_site_mcs">Multiple Cloning Site (MCS)</a> - A designed stretch of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) with recognition sites for many common [restriction enzymes](#restriction_enzyme). This region allows for the easy design, management, and [cloning](#cloning_molecular_cloning) of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) into larger environments, such as [plasmids](#plasmid).

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_n_negative-autoregulation.mdx'
letter: 'n'
word: 'negative-autoregulation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['transcription' ,'positve_autoregulation' ,'concentration']
linkedFrom: ['positive_autoregulation']
---

<a id="negative_autoregulation">Negative Autoregulation</a> - A common regulatory network motif where the result of a process represses itself. An example would a repressor that represses its own [transcription](#transcription). Negative autorgulation can be harnessed to achieve faster convergence to steady state without the energetic waste of increased degradation i.e. [positive autoregulation](#positve_autoregulation). It can also increase the stability of a species [concentrations](#concentration) or induce oscillations depending on parameters.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="network">Network</a> - A group of two or more interacting [sub-units](#subUnit). Each [sub-units](#subUnit) is called a node and the interactions between nodes are termed edges. Networks can be used to describe many different systems. [Protein-protein](#protein) interaction networks have [proteins](#protein) as nodes and the edges between them can be binding interactions. Microbiome studies may describe microbial species as nodes and define the edges as influences on growth rate.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="neuron">Neuron</a> - A specialised cell that can react to stimuli and transmit impulses. A neuron consists of a body which contains the nucleus; dendrites, which are short branches off the body that receive incoming impulses; and a long axon which carries impulses away from the body and to the next neuron.

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_n_nuclease.mdx'

linksTo: ['enzyme' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'backbone' ,'rna' ,'nuclease' ,'methylation' ,'endonuclease' ,'exonuclease']

---

<a id="nuclease">Nuclease</a> - An [enzyme](#enzyme) that creates a cut in the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) [backbone](#backbone); [RNA](#rna) in some cases. Some [nucleases](#nuclease) are sequence specific, others are not. Some depend on the [methylation](#methylation) state or other modifications of the substrate [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). There are two main categories of nucleases, see [endonuclease](#endonuclease), and [exonuclease](#exonuclease).

<a id="nucleic_base_base">Nucleic Base (Base)</a> - In biology this refers to the basic building blocks of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) and [RNA](#rna). The primary nucleobases (nucleic bases) are **Cytosine (C), Guanine (G), Adenine (A), Thymine (T) and Uracil (U)**.

<a id="nucleoside">Nucleoside</a> - A glycosylamine that is can be thought of as a [nucleotide](#nucleotide) without any [phosphate groups](#phosphateGroup). This term is commonly seen in the form of [desoxynucleoside triphosphates (dNTPs)](#desoxynucleosideTriphosphates), a necessary reagent for [PCR reactions](#polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_n_nucleotide.mdx'
letter: 'n'
word: 'nucleotide'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'rna' ,'nitrogenous_base' ,'sugar' ,'ribose' ,'desoxyribose' ,'phosphateGroup' ,'ribonucleotides']
linkedFrom: ['anticodon','antisense_sequence','base_pair_bp','dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid','de_novo','monomer','motif','nucleoside','oligo_oligomer_oligonucleotide','oligo_oligomer_oligonucleotide','oligo_oligomer_oligonucleotide','primer','processitivity','rna','rna','ribonucleotides','sense_sequence','sequence','tale_taler_talen','trna','trna','5_prime_end_5']
---

<a id="nucleotide">Nucleotide</a> - The monomeric unit of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) and [RNA](#rna). A nucleotide comprises: A [nitrogenous base](#nitrogenous_base), a five-carbon [sugar](#sugar) ([ribose](#ribose) or [desoxyribose](#desoxyribose)), at least one [phosphate group](#phosphateGroup) and an organic base. See [ribonucleotide](#ribonucleotides) for related.

 A nucleotide is made of 3 parts:

1. [Nitrogenous base](#nitrogenous_base)
2. Five-carbon [sugar](#sugar); [ribose](#ribose) or [desoxyribose](#desoxyribose)
3. One minimum [phosphate group](#phosphateGroup)

 These single units, nucleotides, are the units by which large nucleic acids DNA/RNA are constructed by polymerisation.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_n_nucleus.mdx'
letter: 'n'
word: 'nucleus'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['membraneBound' ,'eukaryota' ,'cell' ,'gene' ,'molecule']
linkedFrom: ['bacteria','eukaryota','prokaryote']
---

<a id="nucleus">Nucleus</a> - A [membrane-bound](#membraneBound) compartment found in most [eukaryotic cells](#eukaryota). It typically contains most of the [cell](#cell)'s [genetic](#gene) information. This is the site of DNA replication and RNA synthesis. The entrance and exit of large [molecules](#molecule) to and from the nucleus is mediated by nuclear pore complexes in the nuclear membrane.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="nutrient">Nutrient</a> - Any element or simple compound necessary for the health and survival of an organism. This includes air and water, as well as food.

---
fileName: 'biology_ecology_n_nutrient-cycling.mdx'
