<a id="nutrient_cycling">Nutrient Cycling</a> - All the processes by which nutrients are transferred from one organism to another. For instance, the carbon cycle includes uptake of carbon dioxide by plants, ingestion by animals, and respiration and decay of the animal.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_o_oligo-oligomer-oligonucleotide.mdx'
letter: 'o'
word: 'oligo-oligomer-oligonucleotide'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['polymer' ,'nucleotide' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'primer' ,'polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr' ,'southern_blot']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="oligo_oligomer_oligonucleotide">Oligo (Oligomer/Oligonucleotide)</a> - Short [polymers](#polymer) of [nucleotides](#nucleotide) usually less than 200 [nucleotides](#nucleotide) in length. They are typically chemically synthesized and have many uses in biotechnology. [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) oligos can be used as [primers](#primer) for [PCR](#polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr), targets in [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) microarrays, and as probes for [Southern blots](#southern_blot). Oligonucleotides can also refer to very short strands of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) composed of some 10 [nucleotides](#nucleotide).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="operator">Operator</a> - The sequence of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) to which a [transcription factor](#transcription_factor_tf) binds. Operators sequences can be varied to alter the binding affinity of their respective [transcription factor](#transcription_factor_tf).

fileName: 'biology_zoology_o_organ.mdx'
letter: 'o'
word: 'organ'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="organ">Organ</a> - Collection of tissues which performs a particular function or set of functions in an animal or plant's body. The heart, brain, and skin are three organs found in most animals. The leaf, stem, and root are three organs found in most plants. Organs are composed of tissues, and may be organized into larger organ systems.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_o_organ-system.mdx'
letter: 'o'
word: 'organ-system'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="organ_system">Organ System</a> - Collection of organs which have related roles in an organism's functioning. The nervous system, vascular system, and muscle system are all organ systems.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_cellular-biology_o_organelle.mdx'
letter: 'o'
word: 'organelle'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'cellular-biology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['eukaryota']
---

<a id="organelle">Organelle</a> - A membrane-bound structure in a eukaryotic cell that partitions the cell into regions which carry out different cellular functions, e.g., mitochondria, endoplasmic reticulum, lysosomes.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="organic">Organic</a> - Pertaining to compounds containing carbon. Also refers to living things or the materials made by living things. ant. - *inorganic*.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_o_origin-of-replication-ori.mdx'
letter: 'o'
word: 'origin-of-replication-ori'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['plasmid' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'gene']
linkedFrom: ['plasmid','propagation','replication','replicon']
---

<a id="origin_of_replication_ori">Origin of Replication (ORI)</a> - The location in a genome (or within a replicating [plasmid](#plasmid)) at which [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) replication is initiated. [Genes](#gene) near origins of replication will typically have higher copy numbers on average.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

linksTo: ['synthetic_biology']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="oscillator">Oscillator</a> - A biomolecular system characterised by the periodic rise and fall of chemical species. Canonical [synthetic biology](#synthetic_biology) include the metabolator and the repressilator.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="osculum">Osculum</a> - The main opening through which filtered water is discharged. Found in sponges.

---

<a id="ossification">Ossification</a> - The process of bone formation. Special cells called osteoblasts secrete minerals that combine with a network of collagen fibers, forming the hard bone matrix.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="outgroup">Outgroup</a> - In a cladistic analysis, any taxon used to help resolve the polarity of characters, and which is hypothesized to be less closely related to each of the taxa under consideration than any are to each other.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="ovary">Ovary</a> - In flowering plants, the part of the flower which encloses the ovules. When the ovary matures, it becomes the fruit.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_o_overhang.mdx'
letter: 'o'
word: 'overhang'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'doubleStrand' ,'backbone' ,'base_pair_bp']
linkedFrom: ['type_ii_restriction_enzymes']
---

<a id="overhang">Overhang</a> - A short stretch of single-stranded [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) that "hangs off" a region of double-stranded [double-stranded DNA](#doubleStrand). Two overhangs are compatible if they can anneal to form a [double-stranded DNA](#doubleStrand) with no gaps (there can be nicks in the [backbone](#backbone) but no missing [basepairs](#base_pair_bp)).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_o_ovulation.mdx'
letter: 'o'
word: 'ovulation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="ovulation">Ovulation</a> - The process by which an egg (the female gamete) is released from the ovary. In animals other than mammals, with the exception of monotremes, this results in the laying of an egg outside of the body. When female mammals ovulate, the egg, if fertilized, is retained within the uterus.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="ovule">Ovule</a> - In seed plants, the structure which gives rise to the seed.

---

---

<a id="pest_tag">PEST Tag</a> - A [C-terminal](#cTerminalRegion) tag that can be added to [proteins](#protein) to increase their [endogenous](#endogenous) [degradation](#degredation) rate. Termed "PEST" because the peptide is rich in proline (P), glutamate (E), serine (S), and threonine (T).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="paleoherb">Paleoherb</a> - Any member of a group of basal flowering herbs which may be the closest relatives of the monocots. They include the water lilies, Piperales, and Aristolochiales.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="paraphyletic">Paraphyletic</a> - Term applied to a group of organisms which includes the most recent common ancestor of all of its members, but not all of the descendants of that most recent common ancestor.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

---

<a id="parapodia">Parapodia</a> - A sort of "false foot" formed by extension of the body cavity. Polychaetes and some insect larvae have parapodia in addition to their legs, and these provide extra help in locomotion.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="parasite">Parasite</a> - An organism that lives on or within a host (another organism); it obtains nutrients from the host without benefiting or killing (although it may damage) the host.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

<a id="paratope_antigen_binding_site">Paratope (Antigen Binding Site)</a> - This is the part of an antibody which affixes itself to the [antigen](#antigen), it is composed of a small region of around 5 to 10 [amino acids](#amino_acid). For relevent information see [epitope](#epitope_antigenic_determinant).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="parenchyma">Parenchyma</a> - A generalized cell or tissue in a plant. These cells may manufacture or store food, and can often divide or differentiate into other kinds of cells.

---

<a id="parsimony">Parsimony</a> - Refers to a rule used to choose among possible cladograms, which states that the cladogram implying the least number of changes in character states is the best.

---

<a id="pathway">Pathway</a> - A series of interactions among [molecules](#molecule) in a [cell](#cell) that result in a certain product or change in the [cell](#cell). An example is a metabolic pathway where a linked-set of chemical reactions, [catalysed](#catalysation) by enzymes, result in a product or set of products.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="pedipalps">Pedipalps</a> - The second pair of appendages of cheliceromorphs. In many arachnids, such as spiders, the pedipalps are enlarged in the male and used for copulation.

<a id="pelagic">Pelagic</a> - Pelagic organisms swim through the ocean, and may rise to the surface, or sink to the bottom. They are not confined to live on the bottom as benthic organisms do.

<a id="peptidoglycan">Peptidoglycan</a> - carbohydrate polymer cross-linked by proteins. It is found in the cell wall of Gram positive bacteria, where it stains with the dye crystal-violet.

---

<a id="peristome">Peristome</a> - A set of cells or cell parts which surround the opening of a moss sporangium. In many mosses, they are sensitive to humidity, and will alter their shape to aid in spore dispersal.

---

<a id="petal">Petal</a> - One of the outer appendages of a flower, located between the outer sepals and the stamens. Petals often display bright colours that serve to attract pollinators.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_p_petri-dish.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'petri-dish'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['cell_culture' ,'lysogeny_broth' ,'Agar' ,'bacteria' ,'eukaryota']
linkedFrom: ['bacterial_colony','cell_culture','Î²_galactosidase_lactase_Î²_gal_beta_gal']
---

<a id="petri_dish">Petri Dish</a> - A petri dish is a small container used often for [cell cultures](#cell_culture). It is cylindrical and short, normally about 8.5 cm in diameter, and 1.5 cm in height. In microbiology Petri dishes are prepared with variants of [lysogeny broth](#lysogeny_broth) with [agar](#Agar) which solidifies the medium into a gell. This is used for growing [bacterial cells](#bacteria); other mediums are used for [eukaryotic](#eukaryota) or other organisms.  
 Fo more information on Petri dish preparation follow the link: Petri Dish Preparation.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_p_pharyngeal-slits.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'pharyngeal-slits'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="pharyngeal_slits">Pharyngeal Slits</a> - Characteristic of chordates, pharyngeal slits are openings through which water is taken into the pharynx, or throat. In primitive chordates the pharyngeal slits are used to strain water and filter out food particles; in fishes they are modified for respiration. Most terrestrial vertebrates have pharyngeal slits only in the embryonic stage.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="pharynx">Pharynx</a> - Cavity in the digestive tract just past the mouth itself. May be muscularized for sucking or swallowing in various animals.

<a id="phylogenetics">Phylogenetics</a> - Field of biology that deals with the relationships between organisms. It includes the discovery of these relationships, and the study of the causes behind this pattern.

---

<a id="phylogeny">Phylogeny</a> - The evolutionary relationships among organisms; the patterns of lineage branching produced by the true evolutionary history of the organisms being considered.

<a id="placenta">Placenta</a> - In mammals, a tissue formed within the uterus through which nutrients are passed from the mother to the embryo (and later the fetus) and its wastes are removed. It is analogous to the protective membranes in the egg of other amniotes. placental. A mammal that gives live birth to well-developed young that have prolonged embryonic development within the motherâs uterus. Marsupial mammals also have a placenta, but the embryo spends less time developing in the uterus before birth. Placentals include animals as diverse as humans, elephants, dogs, and mice.

---

<a id="plasmid">Plasmid</a> - A relatively small circular piece of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) found in prokaryotes. These pieces of DNA are versatile and can be exchanged intra-species and inter-species; horizontal and vertical exchange respecitively.

 These are usually on the order of tens of kilobases or less. Typical features of a plasmid include the [origin of replication (ORI)](#origin_of_replication_ori), a multiple cloning site, and a marker; such as an antibiotic resistance gene (in a lab setting).

<a id="polarity_of_characters">Polarity Of Characters</a> - The states of characters used in a cladistic analysis, either original or derived.Original characters are those acquired by an ancestor deeper in the phylogeny than the most recent common ancestor of the taxa under consideration. Derived characters are those acquired by the most recent common ancestor of the taxa under consideration.

This may be accomplished by the use of wind, water, insects, birds, bats, or other means. Pollination is usually followed by fertilization, in which sperm are released from the pollen grain to unite with the egg cell.

---

<a id="positive_autoregulation">Positive Autoregulation</a> - A regulatory motif where a [gene](#gene) product activates its own production. This motif can exhibit bistability if a [gene](#gene)'s [basal](#Basal) production rate is below its switching threshold. Compared to [negative autoregulation](#negative_autoregulation) a system exhibiting positive autoregulation will take longer to converge to a given steady state.

<a id="precocial">Precocial</a> - Describes young that are mobile and fairly self-sufficient at birth. Precocial young are generally well-developed (and large) at birth, born with their eyes open, and able to walk. Chickens and grebes are examples of precocial birds; sheep and guinea pigs are examples of precocial mammals.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_p_primer.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'primer'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'dna_polymerase' ,'polymerase' ,'nucleotide' ,'3_prime_end_3' ,'elongation' ,'polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr']
linkedFrom: ['oligo_oligomer_oligonucleotide','processitivity']
---

<a id="primer">Primer</a> - A short, single-stranded [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) used in [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) replication. A primer binds a region of single-stranded [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) to form a primer-template complex which allows [DNA polymerase](#dna_polymerase) to synthesise the complementary strand (primer extension). Since most [DNA polymerases](#polymerase) are only able to catalyse the addition of a [nucleotide](#nucleotide) to the [3'](#3_prime_end_3) end of a [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) strand, primers are necessary for [elongation](#elongation). Primers are a necessary reagent for [PCR](#polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_phylogenetics_p_primitive.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'primitive'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'phylogenetics'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="primitive">Primitive</a> - Describes a character state that is present in the common ancestor of a clade. A primitive character state is inferred to be the original condition of that character within the clade under consideration. For example, "presence of hair" is a primitive character state for all mammals, whereas the "hairlessness" of whales is a derived state for one subclade within the Mammalia.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_p_proboscis.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'proboscis'

dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="proboscis">Proboscis</a> - Elongated organ, usually associated with the mouth. The proboscis is an important feeding appendage in echiurans.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_p_processitivity.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'processitivity'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['enzyme' ,'polymer' ,'catalysation' ,'Subunit' ,'dna_polymerase' ,'primer' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'nucleotide' ,'exonuclease' ,'helicase']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="processitivity">Processitivity</a> - An [enzyme](#enzyme) is processive if it acts on a [polymeric substrate](#polymer) and [catalyses](#catalysation) a reaction on several of the monomeric [subunits](#Subunit) after binding the [polymer](#polymer). For example, [DNA polymerase](#dna_polymerase) is a processive enzyme, as it binds the [primer-template](#primer) complex and then proceeds to create a new strand of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) by moving along the template. Higher processivity means that the [enzyme](#enzyme) stays and acts on the [polymer](#polymer) for longer. *Exempli gratia* a [DNA polymerase](#dna_polymerase) can process thousands of [nucleotides](#nucleotide) after a single binding event. Other processive [enzymes](#enzyme) include some [exonucleases](#exonuclease) which constantly chew up the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid), base by base and [helicases](#helicase) which unwind double-stranded [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_ecology_p_producer.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'producer'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'ecology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="producer">Producer</a> - Any organism which brings energy into an ecosystem from inorganic sources. Most plants and many protists are producers.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_p_prokaryote.mdx'

word: 'prokaryote'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

linksTo: ['nucleus' ,'bacteria']

---

<a id="prokaryote">Prokaryote</a> - An organism without a [nucleus](#nucleus), *exempli gratia* [bacteria](#bacteria).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_cellular-biology_p_prokaryotic.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'prokaryotic'

dataSource: 'berkeley'

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="prokaryotic">Prokaryotic</a> - Literally "before the nucleus", the term applies to all bacteria and archaea. Prokaryotic cells have no internal membranes or cytoskeleton. Their DNA is circular, not linear.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_p_promoter.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'promoter'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'expression' ,'gene' ,'promoter' ,'3_prime_end_3' ,'5_prime_end_5']
linkedFrom: ['activator','ahl','cag_promoter_pcag','constitutive','cooperativity','cytomegalovirus_cmv','operon','promoter','rna_polymerase_rna_p','regulatory_element','reporter','reporter','repressor','reversed_tetracycline_trans_activator_r_tta','reversed_tetracycline_trans_activator_r_tta','tetracycline_trans_activator_tta','tetracycline_trans_activator_tta','tetracycline_responsive_element_tre_ptre','tetracycline_responsive_element_tre_ptre','tetracycline_responsive_element_tre_ptre','transcription','transcription_factor_tf','transcription_factor_tf','transcriptional_fusion','upstream','upstream_activation_sequence_uas_puas','upstream_activation_sequence_uas_puas']
---

<a id="promoter">Promoter</a> - A region of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) that drives the [expression](#expression) of a [gene](#gene) following it on a piece of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). Most [promoters](#promoter) are directional, meaning they drive the expression of a [gene](#gene) only on one side ([3'](#3_prime_end_3)) of it. Some [promoters](#promoter) are bidirectionally driven and will drive the expression on both the [5'](#5_prime_end_5) and [3'](#3_prime_end_3) side.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_p_propagation.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'propagation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['plasmid' ,'host' ,'origin_of_replication_ori' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'cellLine']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="propagation">Propagation</a> - In terms of [plasmids](#plasmid), propagation is the ability of a [plasmid](#plasmid) to be replicated by its [host](#host) organism. A properly-propagating [plasmid](#plasmid) will have an [origin of replication](#origin_of_replication_ori) that is able to recruit the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) replication machinery of the organism. A [plasmid](#plasmid) that does not propagate will ultimately be diluted out of a replicating [cell line](#cellLine) due to cellular divisions.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_p_protease.mdx'
letter: 'p'
word: 'protease'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['enzyme' ,'catalysation' ,'cleavage' ,'peptideBond' ,'protein']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="protease">Protease</a> - An [enzyme](#enzyme) that [catalyses](#catalysation) the [cleavage](#cleavage) of [peptide bonds](#peptideBond); proteases chew up [proteins](#protein).

<a id="protein">Protein</a> - A [polymer](#polymer) of [amino acids](#amino_acid) that typically folds into a particular shape; though [proteins](#protein) with less-defined shapes exist. Some [proteins](#protein) are multimeric, meaning they are a complex of many copies of the same [amino acid](#amino_acid) sequences.

Protein strucutre, primary structure is the sequence of amino acids, secondary Î± helices and Î² sheets, tertiary structure the association of secondary strucutres and quaternary strucutres the association of tertiary structures.

 Many [proteins](#protein) are [enzymes](#enzyme), allowing them to [catalyse](#catalysation) specific reactions, others are structural. [Proteins](#protein) are created in the process of [translation](#translation) using information encoded by [codons](#codon) in a [messenger RNA](#mrna). Note that "natural" amino acids are L-amino acids (levogyre).

dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="pseudoextinction">Pseudoextinction</a> - The apparent disappearance of a taxon. In cases of pseudoextinction, this disappearance is not due to the death of all members, but the evolution of novel features in one or more lineages, so that the new clades are not recognized as belonging to the paraphyletic ancestral group, whose members have ceased to exist. The Dinosauria, if defined so as to exclude the birds, is an example of a group that has undergone pseudoextinction.

<a id="pteridophyte">Pteridophyte</a> - Plant in which the sporophyte generation is the larger phase and in which the gametophyte lives an existence independent of its parent sporophyte. Pteridophytes are almost all vascular plants, and include the lycophytes, trimerophytes, sphenophytes, and ferns.

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="quantitative_polymerase_chain_reaction_qpcr">Quantitative Polymerase Chain Reaction (qPCR)</a> - [Quantitative](#quantitative) [PCR](#polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr). A method of determining the amount of a [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) sequence of interest that is present in a sample. By monitoring the [amplification](#amplification) of a strand of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) during [PCR](#polymerase_chain_reaction_pcr), the original quantity can be [extrapolated](#extrapolation). qPCR can be used to monitor [gene expression](#geneExpression) by [reverse transcribing](#rtpcr) [mRNA](#rna) into [cDNA](#rtpcr) and then [quantifying](#quantitative) the [cDNA](#cdna) through qPCR.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_q_quorum-sensing.mdx'
letter: 'q'
word: 'quorum-sensing'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['molecule' ,'synthetic_biology']
linkedFrom: ['ahl','lasi','lux_system_luxi_luxr']
---

<a id="quorum_sensing">Quorum Sensing</a> - The ability of an organism to detect population density of others and or a [molecule](#molecule). The canonical quorum sensing system is the AHL-Lux system first described in *Aliivibrio fischeri* (formerly classified as *Vibrio fischeri*). Quorum sensing systems have been co-opted by [synthetic biologists](#synthetic_biology) to engineer cell-to-cell communication systems.

linksTo: ['polymer' ,'nucleotide' ,'mrna' ,'catalysation' ,'ribozyme' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'protein' ,'doubleStrand' ,'nitrogenous_base' ,'desoxyribose' ,'ribose' ,'rrna' ,'phylogeny']
linkedFrom: ['alphavirus','aptamer','base_pair_bp','chromatin','complementary','desoxyribose','electrophoresis','endonuclease','gene','hairpin','ligand','ligase_ligation','machine','mirna','mrna','nitrogenous_base','nuclease','nucleic_base_base','nucleotide','open_reading_frame_orf','positive_rna_rna','quantitative_polymerase_chain_reaction_qpcr','rna_binding_protein_rna_bp','rna_binding_protein_rna_bp','rna_interference_rnai','rna_polymerase_rna_p','rna_seq','regulatory_element','replicon','replicon','rtpcr','rtpcr','ribonucleotides','ribose','ribosome','ribosome_binding_site_rbs','ribozyme','ribozyme','rrna','scaffold','scaffold','sense_sequence','shrna','shrna','sirna','strand','terminator','terminator','terminator','transcription','transcriptional_fusion','transcriptome','trna','trna','vesicle','virus','virus','3_prime_end_3','5_prime_end_5']
---

<a id="rna">RNA</a> - Ribonucleic acid; [polymeric molecules](#polymer) made up of [nucleotide](#nucleotide) monomers. RNA has many biological functions from information carrying ([mRNA](#mrna)) to [catalytic](#catalysation) activity ([ribozymes](#ribozyme)); its primary function however, is to transmit information from longterm storage ([DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid)) to active machinery [proteins](#protein). RNA is often found folded unto itself instead of in a [double strand](#doubleStrand) type; which is often the case with [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). RNA is composed of 4 different kinds of [nucleotides](#nucleotide) with the [nitrogenous bases](#nitrogenous_base): A (Adenine), U (Uracil), C (Cytosine), and G (Guanine). RNA notably contains U instead of T (thymine) as [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) does. RNA also does not contain [desoxyribose](#desoxyribose) as [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) does but [ribose](#ribose) instead. The 18S [ribosomal RNA](#rrna) sequence has been used in many groups of organisms to reconstruct [phylogeny](#phylogeny).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_rna-binding-protein-rna-bp.mdx'
letter: 'r'
word: 'rna-binding-protein-rna-bp'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['protein' ,'rna' ,'transcription' ,'green_fluorescent_protein_gfp_egfp' ,'mrna']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="rna_binding_protein_rna_bp">RNA Binding Protein (RNA-BP)</a> - A [protein](#protein) that binds to an [RNA](#rna) sequence as its substrate. Naturally, these [proteins](#protein) serve a variety of roles in post-[transcriptional](#transcription) regulation. Recently, bacteriophage coat [proteins](#protein) such as PP7 and MS2 have been used to target [RNA](#rna) sequences that have had RBP binding sites integrated into them. Fusion of these RBPs to [fluorescent proteins](#green_fluorescent_protein_gfp_egfp) allows the real-time monitoring of [mRNA](#mrna) [transcription](#transcription).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_rna-interference-rnai.mdx'
letter: 'r'
word: 'rna-interference-rnai'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['doubleStrand' ,'rna' ,'inhibitor' ,'gene' ,'rna_interference_rnai' ,'virus' ,'vector' ,'sirna' ,'eukaryota' ,'sachharomyces_cerevisiae' ,'prokaryote']
linkedFrom: ['mirna','rna_interference_rnai','sachharomyces_cerevisiae','yeast','yeast']
---

<a id="rna_interference_rnai">RNA Interference (RNAi)</a> - A biological process by which [double-stranded](#doubleStrand) [RNA](#rna) (dsRNA) [inhibits](#inhibitor) the expression of [genes](#gene) complementary to its sequence. [RNAi](#rna_interference_rnai) is thought to have evolved as a defense against [viruses](#virus) (some of which have dsRNA genomes) and it has been shown to have an important role during development. This system can also be exploited to induce artificial gene knockdown through the introduction of synthetic dsRNAs or [vectors](#vector) that express [siRNAs](#sirna).

While most [eukaryotes](#eukaryota) have [RNAi](#rna_interference_rnai) machinery, [*S. cerevisiae*](#sachharomyces_cerevisiae) notably lacks it. [Prokaryotes](#prokaryote) also do not possess [RNAi](#rna_interference_rnai) machinery.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_rna-polymerase-rna-p.mdx'
letter: 'r'
word: 'rna-polymerase-rna-p'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['protein' ,'transcription' ,'rna' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'promoter' ,'specificity' ,'base_pair_bp' ,'codon' ,'gene' ,'transcription_factor_tf' ,'repressor' ,'eukaryota' ,'mrna' ,'tRNA' ,'rrna' ,'regulatory_rna']
linkedFrom: ['activator','tale_taler_talen','terminator']
---

<a id="rna_polymerase_rna_p">RNA Polymerase (RNA-P)</a> - RNA polymerase; the [protein](#protein) complex that [transcribes](#transcription) [RNA](#rna) from [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). In prokaryotes RNA-P, [promoter](#promoter) [specificity](#specificity) is determined by the presence of a sigma factor and the complex usually binds to the -35 and -10 elements (35[bp](#base_pair_bp) and 10[bp](#base_pair_bp) upstream of the start [codon](#codon)) of [genes](#gene). Occlusion of these sites through [transcription factor](#transcription_factor_tf) binding is a common mechanism of genetic [repression](#repressor). In [eukaryotes](#eukaryota), [mRNA](#mrna) [transcription](#transcription) is carried out by RNA polymerase II, but other RNA-P types are responsible for the production of [transfer RNAs (tRNA)](#tRNA), [ribosomal RNAs (rRNA)](#rrna), and some regulatory [RNAs](#regulatory_rna).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_rna-seq.mdx'
letter: 'r'
word: 'rna-seq'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['rna' ,'sequencing' ,'transcription' ,'mrna' ,'cell' ,'PolyATail' ,'rtpcr' ,'next_gen_sequencing' ,'transcriptome']
linkedFrom: ['transcriptome','transcriptome']
---

<a id="rna_seq">RNA-Seq</a> - [RNA](#rna) [sequencing](#sequencing). A method of obtaining a snapshot of genetic [transcripts](#transcription) present in an organism. [mRNA](#mrna)s can be isolated from a [cell](#cell) by their [polyA tail](#PolyATail) and then [reverse transcribed](#rtpcr) into [cDNA](#rtpcr). [Next-generation sequencing](#next_gen_sequencing) methods can then be used to [sequence](#sequencing) this [cDNA](#rtpcr), which allows the reconstruction of the [cell](#cell)'s [transcriptome](#transcriptome).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="radiation">Radiation</a> - Event of rapid cladogenesis, believed to occur under conditions where a new feature permits a lineage to move into a new niche or new habitat, and is then called an adaptive radiation.

<a id="rain_shadow">Rain Shadow</a> - The dry region on the leeward side of a mountain range, where rainfall is noticeably less than on the windward side. For example, the White Mountains in east central California are in the rain shadow of the Sierra Nevada.

<a id="rank">Rank</a> - In traditional taxonomy, taxa are ranked according to their level of inclusiveness. Thus a genus contains one or more species, a family includes one or more genera, and so on.

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_rate-of-change.mdx'

dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="rate_of_change">Rate of Change</a> - How much a dependent variable changes for a given change in an independent variable. Graphically, it is the slope of a line where the independent variable is on the x-axis and the dependent variable is on the y. The rate of change at any point can be determined by taking the first derivative of a function with respect to the independent variable.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="rbcl">RbcL</a> - a gene which is located in the chloroplast of photosynthetic organisms. It codes for the large subunit of the protein rubisco, and its sequence has been useful in plant phylogenies.

<a id="recognition_site">Recognition Site</a> - The specific sequence recognised by a [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid)\-binding protein. Most commonly referred to when discussing the cut sites for [restriction enzymes](#restriction_enzyme).

<a id="recombination">Recombination</a> - The insertion or deletion of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) sequence from a strand mediated by recombinases (enzymes which catalyse recombination). **Cre** Recombinase, from a bacteriophage, is a commonly-used recombinase that affects site-specific recombination between two [LOX sites](#loxSite). Recombination is the basis of [Gateway cloning technology](#golden_gate).

<a id="regulatory_element">Regulatory Element</a> - Any element that regulates [gene expression](#geneExpression). Examples of [cis](#trans_cis)\-acting regulatory elements are operators, [promotors](#promoter), and leader peptides. [Trans](#trans_cis)\-acting regulatory elements are [diffusible molecules](#diffusion) such as [transcription factors](#transcription_factor_tf) or [trans](#trans_cis)\-acting [RNA](#rna) in a toehold switch system.

<a id="replication">Replication</a> - The process of producing two identical copies of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) from a single [double helix](#doubleStrand). [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) replication begins at specific sequences termed [origins of replication](#origin_of_replication_ori) and requires [polymerases](#polymerase), [dNTPs](#desoxynucleosideTriphosphates), and other factors.

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="replicon">Replicon</a> - A [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) or [RNA molecule](#rna) that replicates from a single [origin of replication](#origin_of_replication_ori). Most [prokaryotic](#prokaryote) [chromosomes](#chromosome) are a single replicon, while [eukaryotic](#eukaryota) [chromosomes](#chromosome) typically have multiple replicons. "Replicon" is sometimes used to describe self-amplifying [RNA](#rna)s (RepRNA), which have the ability to replicate themselves within a [transfected](#transfection) [cell](#cell) to provide continuous [protein](#protein) production.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_reporter.mdx'
letter: 'r'
word: 'reporter'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['geneExpression' ,'transcription' ,'promoter' ,'phenotype' ,'lacz' ,'x_gal' ,'fluorescence' ,'green_fluorescent_protein_gfp_egfp' ,'quantitative' ,'protein']
linkedFrom: ['Î²_galactosidase_lactase_Î²_gal_beta_gal']
---

<a id="reporter">Reporter</a> - In the context of [gene expression](#geneExpression), a reporter allows the easy determination of [transcription](#transcription) from a given [promoter](#promoter). Good reporters have an obvious [phenotype](#phenotype) such as the blue [phenotype](#phenotype) for [LacZ](#lacz) in the presence of [X-gal](#x_gal), or the [fluorescence](#fluorescence) of a [fluorescent protein](#green_fluorescent_protein_gfp_egfp). [Quantification](#quantitative) of [protein](#protein) production from a [promoter](#promoter) as a function of reporter [fluorescence](#fluorescence) is also possible.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_repressilator.mdx'

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="repressilator">Repressilator</a> - One of the earliest oscillating synthetic circuits published by Elowitz and Leibler in 2000\. It accomplishes oscillations through the use of a three-repressor ring oscillator circuit topology. The circuit was able to oscillate, but had issues with robustness.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="repressor">Repressor</a> - The suppression of [gene expression](#geneExpression) from a [promoter](#promoter) by a [protein](#protein). Important repressors in [synthetic biology](#synthetic_biology) are TetR, [LacI](#laci), and cI (lambda repressor). Some repressors are inducible.

<a id="response">Response</a> - How a system reacts to an input. Much information about a system's internal workings can be gleaned from observing its response to different types of input.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_restriction-enzyme.mdx'
letter: 'r'
word: 'restriction-enzyme'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['enzyme' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'cloning_molecular_cloning' ,'golden_gate']
linkedFrom: ['biobrick','bsai','golden_gate','multiple_cloning_site_mcs','recognition_site','type_ii_restriction_enzymes']
---

<a id="restriction_enzyme">Restriction Enzyme</a> - [Enzymes](#enzyme) that cut [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) in a site-specific manner. Typically, each restriction enzyme has a certain restriction site that it recognises. Standard restriction enzymes that cut within their recognition site are the basis of traditional [cloning](#cloning_molecular_cloning) methods. Type IIS restriction enzymes, such BsaI, cut at a location outside of their recognition site and enable [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) assembly without the producing scar regions. Type IIS restriction enzymes are the basis of [Golden Gate cloning](#golden_gate) methods.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="reversed_tetracycline_trans_activator_r_tta">Reversed Tetracycline Trans-Activator (r-tTA)</a> - Analogous to tTA, except that the function of [DOX](#doxycycline_dox) is reversed. [DOX](#doxycycline_dox) stabilises the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) binding domain, facilitating [promoter](#promoter) binding and activation of [gene expression](#geneExpression) of [promoters](#promoter) with tetracycline responsive elements (TREs). Referred to as the DOX-on system.

<a id="ribonucleotides">Ribonucleotides</a> - Same as a [nucleotide](#nucleotide) yet includes [ribose](#ribose) instead of [dextrose](#dextrose) as the [sugar](#sugar) component to the nucleic material; one is of course [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) and the other [RNA](#rna).

<a id="ribose">Ribose</a> - Ribose is a form of sugar, this kind is special in that it is included in genetic material of the [RNA](#rna) kind. [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) includes another kind known as [dextrose](#dextrose).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

linksTo: ['rna' ,'translation' ,'mrna' ,'Polypeptide' ,'protein']

<a id="ribosome">Ribosome</a> - A protein-[RNA](#rna) complex that is responsible for [translating](#translation) [mRNA](#mrna) into [polypeptides](#Polypeptide) i.e. [proteins](#protein).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_ribosome-binding-site-rbs.mdx'
letter: 'r'
word: 'ribosome-binding-site-rbs'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['codon' ,'ribosome' ,'translation' ,'prokaryote' ,'eukaryota' ,'protein' ,'rna' ,'conformation']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="ribosome_binding_site_rbs">Ribosome Binding Site (RBS)</a> - A sequence upstream of the start [codon](#codon) that recruits [ribosomes](#ribosome) and allows [translation](#translation). RBSs are well-defined in [prokaryotic](#prokaryote) systems and are also known as Shine-Dalgarno sequences. Recruitment of [ribosomes](#ribosome) in [eukaryotic](#eukaryota) systems is more complex and less-understood. RBS "strength" is a large factor in [protein](#protein) production rate and is determined by local [RNA](#rna) [secondary](#conformation) and [tertiary](#conformation) structure. RBS calculators allow the control of relative [translation](#translation) rates across different RBSs.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_r_riboswitch.mdx'

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="riboswitch">Riboswitch</a> - A [cis](#trans_cis)\-acting regulatory element found in [mRNA](#mrna) transcripts. Riboswitches form structures whose [conformations](#conformation) are affected by small [molecules](#molecule). These [conformational](#conformation) changes have the ability to turn expression of a transcript "ON" or "OFF". This switching is accomplished through a variety of mechanisms.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="ribozyme">Ribozyme</a> - An [RNA molecule](#rna) that is capable of [catalysing](#catalysation) chemical reactions. Many ribozymes of interest (hammerhead and hairpin) [catalyse](#catalysation) [RNA](#rna) [cleavage](#cleavage) and [ligation](#ligation) reactions.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_scaffold.mdx'

linksTo: ['enzyme' ,'rna' ,'protein' ,'substrate' ,'diffusion']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="scaffold">Scaffold</a> - A structure on which elements can be brought together to be close in space. For example, the [enzymes](#enzyme) involved in the same pathway can be brought together in proximity on an [RNA scaffold](#rna) by fusing the [enzymes](#enzyme) with [RNA](#rna)\-binding [proteins](#protein) and thus increase the efficiency of the pathway, as [substrates](#substrate) do not need to [diffuse](#diffusion) far to reach the next [enzyme](#enzyme) in the pathway.

<a id="scanning_electron_microscope_sem">Scanning Electron Microscope (SEM)</a> - A special kind of microscope that scans samples with a high-energy beam of electrons to produce a high-resolution, detailed, three-dimensional image. An SEM can magnify a sample up to 250 times that of the best light microscopes.

<a id="screening">Screening</a> - A method to obtain a set of organisms *exempli gratia* a [bacterial colony](#bacterial_colony), with a particular [genotype](#genotype) or [phenotype](#phenotype) by considering many members of a large pool of variants. Each member is assessed for its suitability, causing more work than [selection](#selection), where the undesired members are eliminated.

<a id="secondary_growth">Secondary Growth</a> - Growth in a plant which does not occur at the tips of the stems or roots. Secondary growth produces wood and bark in seed plants.

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_secondary-structure.mdx'

<a id="secondary_structure">Secondary Structure</a> - A secondary structure in a protein refers to the the three dimensional form which a [polypetidic](#protein) chain takes: either [Î± helices](#alpha_helix), [Î² sheets](#betaSheet), Î² turns, and even Ï loops. See [protein](#protein) for an illustration.

 The [primary strucutre](#primaryStructure) refers to the sequence of [amino acids](#amino_acid) composing the chain, and the [tertiary strucutre](#tertiaryStructure) the association of secondary structures.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="segmentation">Segmentation</a> - In many animals, the body is divided into repeated subunits called segments, such as those in centipedes, insects, and annelids. Segmentation is the state of having or developing a body plan in this way.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_selection.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'selection'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['antibiotic_resistance_gene','screening','toxin']
---

<a id="selection">Selection</a> - A phenomena by which organisms reproduce differentially; some more than others. This process results in some genotypes/phenotypes dominating a population.

 Selection can be positive (organisms with a trait survive to the next round) or negative (organisms that do not have a trait survive to the next round).

 In a lab setting this can be used as a method for directed evolution typically with bacteria. This approach can be less work than screening, as only the "interesting" organisms survive, rather than all organisms.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_sense-sequence.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'sense-sequence'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

linksTo: ['positive_rna_rna' ,'rna' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'translation' ,'protein' ,'nucleotide' ,'antisense_sequence']
linkedFrom: ['antisense_sequence','positive_rna_rna','watson_strand_5_3']
---

<a id="sense_sequence">Sense Sequence</a> - [Positive RNA](#positive_rna_rna) is the [RNA](#rna) version of sense [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) (also called positive); this strand would be [translateable](#translation) into a [protein](#protein). A sense sequence of [nucleotides](#nucleotide) is complementary to an [antisense coding sequence](#antisense_sequence).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_sensing.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'sensing'

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="sensing">Sensing</a> - The process of detecting levels of inputs from the outside or within a [cell](#cell).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_sensitivity.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'sensitivity'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['specificity','specificity','specificity']
---

<a id="sensitivity">Sensitivity</a> - How well a method can pick up true positives; calculated by dividing the number of true positives by the number of true positives added to the number of false negatives.

 $$ Sensitivity = \frac{(True Positives)}{(True Positives) + (False Negatives)} $$


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="septum">Septum</a> - Partition which divides up a larger region into smaller ones, such as in the central body cavity of some anthozoa.

<a id="sequence">Sequence</a> - A suite of specific or unique values. In biology a sequence refers to a suite of [nucleotides](#nucleotide) in a certain order; which can define a [gene](#gene).

<a id="shoot">Shoot</a> - Usually, the above ground portion of a plant, bearing the leaves. Contrast with root.

-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="signal">Signal</a> - A function conveying information. A signal can take and be encoded in many forms, *exempli gratia* the voltage of a wire or the concentration of a chemical species. Systems can act on signals to modify them or to produce new signals.

<a id="silica">Silica</a> - amorphous silicon dioxide (glass). It is a structural component in many organisms, such as diatoms and horsetails.

---

<a id="siphon">Siphon</a> - Opening in molluscs or in urochordates which draws water into the body cavity. In many molluscs, the siphon may be used to expel water forcibly, providing a means of propulsion.

---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_s_skeleton.mdx'

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="skeleton">Skeleton</a> - Support structure in animals, against which the force of muscles acts. Vertebrates have a skeleton of bone or cartilage; arthropods have one made of chitin; while many other invertebrates use a hydrostatic skeleton, which is merely an incompressible fluid-filled region of their body.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_southern-blot.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'southern-blot'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'electrophoresis' ,'antibody']
linkedFrom: ['electrophoresis','oligo_oligomer_oligonucleotide']
---

<a id="southern_blot">Southern Blot</a> - A lab technique used for the detection of specific [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) sequences in a sample. Sothern blotting typically involves a first migration by classic [electrophoresis](#electrophoresis) then a "blotting" step by a membrane which uptakes the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) from the gell, then the probe which is complementary to the strand of interest is introduced. This probe is typically marked by a radioactive strand or an [antibody](#antibody). This reveals if the sequence of interest was found in the sample or not.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_ecology_s_specialist.mdx'

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="specialist">Specialist</a> - Organism which has adopted a lifestyle specific to a particular set of conditions. Contrast with generalist.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_species.mdx'

word: 'species'

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['state_variable']
---

<a id="species">Species</a> - A slippery concept contested even today. Current consensus states that a species is a group of like individuals which are capable of reproduction typically by sexual reproduction.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_specificity.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'specificity'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['sensitivity']
linkedFrom: ['aptamer','rna_polymerase_rna_p']
---

<a id="specificity">Specificity</a> - How well a method can distinguish between true positives and false positives; also called the true negative rate and calculated by dividing the number of true negatives by the number of true negatives added to the number of false positives.

 $$ Specificity = \frac{(True Negatives)}{(True Negatives) + (False Positives)} $$

Often at odds with [sensitivity](#sensitivity) (increasing specificity typically decreases [sensitivity](#sensitivity); this can be observed with a receiver operating characteristic curve, which plots 1 minus specificity against [sensitivity](#sensitivity)).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

---

<a id="state_variable">State Variable</a> - A variable dedicated to describing a state of a system, *exempli gratia* the [concentration](#concentration) of a [species](#species), the volume of a [cell](#cell) or any other measurable quantity.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_stateful.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'stateful'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['logic_gate']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="stateful">Stateful</a> - Having a state, having memory. For example, a toggle switch is stateful since it has two states. Combinational [logic circuits](#logic_gate) are not stateful, they do not have any memory of previous inputs or states.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_steady-state.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'steady-state'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['evolution']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="steady_state">Steady State</a> - A state of the system which does not [evolve](#evolution) over time, given that there are no perturbations. Steady states can be stable or unstable, indicating their response to small perturbations (stable means the system returns to the steady state and unstable means it does not).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_phylogenetics_s_stem-group.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'stem-group'

category: 'phylogenetics'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="stem_group">Stem Group</a> - All the taxa in a clade preceding a major cladogenesis event. They are often difficult to recognize because they may not possess synapomorpies found in the crown group.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_botany_s_stigma.mdx'

linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="stigma">Stigma</a> - The sticky tip of a pistil. Or, the dense region of pigments found in many photosynthetic protists which is sensitive to light, and thus functions somewhat like a miniature eye.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_botany_s_stipe.mdx'

<a id="stipules">Stipules</a> - Paired appendages found at the base of the leaves of many flowering plants.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_stochastic.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'stochastic'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="stochastic">Stochastic</a> - Random, non-deterministic. A stochastic model enables modeling of discrete systems containing a small number of species, where deterministic, continuous models may give inappropriate predictions. Stochastic simulations enable predicting properties other than the mean, bulk behaviour of a system. Stochastic simulations can show unexpected properties of systems which deterministic-continuous models might not.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_botany_s_stomata.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'stomata'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'botany'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="stomata">Stomata</a> - Openings in the epidermis of a stem or leaf of a plant which permit gas exchange with the air. In general, all plants except liverworts have stomata in their sporophyte stage.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_strain.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'strain'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['bacteria' ,'virus' ,'escherichia_coli_e_coli' ,'genotype']
linkedFrom: ['e_coli_escherichia_coli_k12_strain','escherichia_coli_e_coli']
---

<a id="strain">Strain</a> - A particular variant of a [bacterium](#bacteria), [virus](#virus) or plant. For example, the [*E. coli*](#escherichia_coli_e_coli) strain BL21(DE3) has a particular [genotype](#genotype) setting it apart from other strains and making it useful for some applications and not others.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_s_strand.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'strand'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'rna' ,'5_prime_end_5' ,'phosphateGroup' ,'3_prime_end_3']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="strand">Strand</a> - A single [DNA molecule](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) or [RNA](#rna). Such a strand has directionality, typically depicted as going from [5'](#5_prime_end_5) (the end of the strand with the [phosphate group](#phosphateGroup)) to [3'](#3_prime_end_3) (the end of the strand with the -OH group).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="subunit">Subunit</a> - Subunit refers to a component part of a whole, this can be used when talking of parts of a multichain protein.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_ecology_s_substrate.mdx'
letter: 's'
word: 'substrate'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'ecology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['affinity','ligase_ligation','scaffold']
---

<a id="substrate">Substrate</a> - "Supporting surface" on which an organism grows. The substrate may simply provide structural support, or may provide water and nutrients. A substrate may be inorganic, such as rock or soil, or it may be organic, such as wood.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_biochemistry_s_sugar.mdx'

<a id="sugar">Sugar</a> - A generic name for soluble [carbohydrate](#carbohydrate) moelcules, often contained in food.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_ecology_s_symbiosis.mdx'

word: 'symbiosis'

category: 'ecology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="symbiosis">Symbiosis</a> - A relationship between two organisms that live in intimate contact with each other; includes mutualism (both organisms benefit, they rely on each other for survival), parasitism (one organism benefits at its host's expense) and commensalism (one partner benefits and the other is neither benefitted nor harmed).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

---

<a id="synapomorphy">Synapomorphy</a> - A character which is derived, and because it is shared by the taxa under consideration, is used to infer common ancestry.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---

linkedFrom: ['biocad','biocompiler','chassis','cytomegalovirus_cmv','homeostasis','oscillator','quorum_sensing','repressor','sachharomyces_cerevisiae','yeast']
---

<a id="synthetic_biology">Synthetic Biology</a> - An interdisciplinary domain of study, focused on engineering and creating novel forms of useful life. 

 Synthetic biology can be applied in industry, medicine, or even artificial intelligence research (wetware). It combines skills from life science, mathematics, engineering, chemistry, physical and computer science. Synthetic biology can be applied in industry, medicine, or even artificial intelligence research (wetware). It combines skills from life science, mathematics, engineering, chemistry, physical and computer science. Synthetic biology can be applied in industry, medicine, or even artificial intelligence research (wetware). It combines skills from life science, mathematics, engineering, chemistry, physical and computer science.

<a id="systematics">Systematics</a> - Field of biology that deals with the diversity of life. Systematics is usually divided into the two areas of phylogenetics and taxonomy.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_tale-taler-talen.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'tale-taler-talen'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['transcription' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'protein' ,'amino_acid' ,'nucleotide' ,'rna_polymerase_rna_p' ,'geneExpression' ,'nuclease']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="tale_taler_talen">TALE, TALER, TALEN</a> - [Transcription](#transcription) activator-like effectors (**TALEs**) are [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) binding [proteins](#protein) that have a "code" relating just two specific [amino acids](#amino_acid) in their [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid)\-binding regions to a [nucleotide](#nucleotide) in the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) that is recognised. This "code" has been used by researchers to create a variety of **TALE** [proteins](#protein) that bind specific [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) operator sites.

**TALE** operator sites can be placed near [transcriptional](#transcription) start sites to block [RNA polymerase](#rna_polymerase_rna_p) binding and thus repress [gene expression](#geneExpression). **TALEs** used for this purpose are called **TALE** repressors, or **TALERs**. **TALEs** can also be modified to have [nuclease activity](#nuclease), and cut [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) at specific locations in the genome. These are refered to **TALE** nucleases, or **TALENs**.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="tag">Tag</a> - A tag enables an experimenter to follow or extract a particular [molecule](#molecule), molecular species or even whole cells. *Exempli gratia* the His-tag enables experimenters to enrich for species containing said tag using columns (a nickel column for the His-tag). [Fluorescent](#fluorescence) tags enable measurement with devices like plate readers or [flow cytometers](#facs).

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_terminator.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'terminator'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

linksTo: ['transcription' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'rna' ,'rna_polymerase_rna_p' ,'protein' ,'polymerase']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="terminator">Terminator</a> - The process of termination is the stopping of [transcription](#transcription). This occurs due to particular sequences, terminator sequences, within the [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). Some terminators cause termination by causing the [RNA](#rna) to fold into structures that cause the [RNA](#rna_polymerase_rna_p) to release it. Others recruit [proteins](#protein) which pull the freshly synthesised (nascent) [RNA](#rna) out of the [RNA](#rna) [polymerase](#polymerase) or cause the release by other mechanisms.

<a id="tetracycline_trans_activator_tta">Tetracycline Trans-activator (tTA)</a> - Is a fusion of a tetracycline-destabilising [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) binding domain and the [VP16](#vp16) [trans-activation domain](#tad). Thus, in the presence of [DOX](#doxycycline_dox) (an analog of tetracycline) tTA can no longer bind to its target [promoter](#promoter)

<a id="tetracycline_responsive_element_tre_ptre">Tetracycline-Responsive Element (TRE/pTRE)</a> - A [promoter](#promoter) that contains operator sequences ([TetO](#teto)) for a [TetR](#tetr) [protein](#protein) to bind. The TRE [promoter](#promoter) contains multiple [TetO](#teto) sites and a minimal [CMV](#cytomegalovirus_cmv) core [promoter](#promoter).

---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_t_tetrapod.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'tetrapod'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="tetrapod">Tetrapod</a> - An animal with four limbs that evolved from a common fish ancestor during the Devonian Period (\~365 million years ago). Tetrapods include amphibians, reptiles, birds, and mammals. Though "tetrapod" literally translates to "four-footed," many animals in this group have limbs adapted for different modes of transportation. Humans walk upright on two legs; the legs of whales, dolphins, and other marine mammals have evolved into fins and flippers; and snakes have lost their legs all together. Tetrapods are generally thought of as terrestrial animals, but some, like dolphins and whales, have returned to marine habitats.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="thalloid">Thalloid</a> - Plants which have no roots, stems, or leaves are called thalloid, such as liverworts and hornworts.

<a id="theca">Theca</a> - General term for any stiff outer covering of a unicellular protist, and usually made up of interlocking plates. dinoflagellates and diatoms are examples of protists with thecae.

<a id="thermolabile">Thermolabile</a> - Refers to a [protein](#protein), [enzyme](#enzyme), or molecule that is (generally) negatively impacted or destroyed/[denatures](#denatures) by heat. An example would be a thermosensitive [origin of replication](#oriR) or a thermolabile T5 [exonuclease](#exonuclease).

<a id="thermostable">Thermostable</a> - Resistant to high temperature. A thermostable [enzyme](#enzyme) is still active at elevated temperatures (*exempli gratia* near boiling) and have been found in organisms that live in extreme environments, *exempli gratia* deep sea thermal vents.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

---

<a id="thorax">Thorax</a> - In insects, the second body region, between the head and thorax. It is the region where the legs and wings are attached.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_tight-junction.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'tight-junction'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['epithelium' ,'apical' ,'ion' ,'diffusion' ,'protein' ,'cell' ,'basolateral']
linkedFrom: ['transactivation_domain_tad']
---

<a id="tight_junction">Tight junction</a> - Intercellular structure which forms an almost perfect continuous seal between two adjacent [epithelial cells](#epithelium) close to their [apical](#apical) (side which faces the lumen) side. The tightness of the seal may vary depending on the kind of [epithelium](#epithelium). It acts as a filter which lets water and some other [ions](#ion) come through and into the organism. These tight junctions are also important in halting the [diffusion](#diffusion) of [proteins](#protein) and cytoplasmique glycolipids from the [apical](#apical) side of the [cell](#cell) to the [basolateral](#basolateral) side.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_timescale-separation.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'timescale-separation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['equilibrium' ,'transcription_factor_tf' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'protein']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="timescale_separation">Timescale Separation</a> - A method for simplifying time-dependent systems. It is often the case that a system has processes which have timescales (how long it takes for the system to reach [equilibrium](#equilibrium)) differing by one or more orders of magnitude. For example, the timescale of [transcription factors](#transcription_factor_tf) binding to [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) is short, as the binding [equilibrium](#equilibrium) is reached within milliseconds or less. However, the process of producing a mature [protein](#protein) can take minutes or more. Hence, when analysing a system where both processes occur, the binding can be considered to be at [equilibrium](#equilibrium) when discussing how [protein](#protein) dynamics look.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_timing-diagram.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'timing-diagram'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['evolution']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="timing_diagram">Timing Diagram</a> - A diagram showing how a system behaves and [evolves](#evolution) over time. For digital systems, a timing diagram shows the state of the system (and possibly signals within the system) at each tick of a clock. Often a timing diagram is depicted as a table, where each row shows a signal and each column shows an instance of time. The value in the table is the value of the particular signal at the particular time. Another way to depict the timing diagram is to draw a value trace over time for each signal and stack them such that time flows left to right.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_t_tissue.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'tissue'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="tissue">Tissue</a> - A group of cells with a specific function in the body of an organism. Lung tissue, vascular tissues, and muscle tissue are all kinds of tissues found in some animals. Tissues are usually composed of similar cells, and are often organized into larger units called organs.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_topology.mdx'
letter: 't'

dataSource: 'original-dereck'

linksTo: ['node' ,'gene']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="topology">Topology</a> - In the context of regulatory networks, the topology refers to the way the [nodes](#node) (*exempli gratia* [genes](#gene)) are connected (which kinds of arrows go from which [nodes](#node) to which [nodes](#node)). An abstract gene-regulatory network has some topology that could be implemented by many ways by choosing the suitable components for each node.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_toxin.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'toxin'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['molecule' ,'protein' ,'selection' ,'bacteria']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="toxin">Toxin</a> - A substance (small [molecule](#molecule), peptide, [protein](#protein)) that kills cells or even whole organisms. Toxin-antitoxin pairs can be useful in biotechnology where the presence of the antitoxin confers resistance to the toxin, enabling [selection](#selection). Producing a toxin as the output of a circuit can be used in medical applications, *exempli gratia* to kill cancerous cells or infectious [bacteria](#bacteria).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_zoology_t_tracheae.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'tracheae'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'zoology'
dataSource: 'berkeley'

published: true

linksTo: ['']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="tracheae">Tracheae</a> - Internal tubes through which air is taken for respiration. Vertebrates with lungs have a single trachea carrying air to the lungs, while insects and some other land-living arthropods have a complex network of tracheae carrying air from the spiracles to all parts of the body.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

fileName: 'biology_botany_t_tracheophyte.mdx'

<a id="tracheophyte">Tracheophyte</a> - Any member of the clade of plants possessing vascular tissue; a vascular plant.

<a id="trans_cis">Trans/Cis</a> - Trans means two things on opposite sides from one another, and cis means to things which are on the same side.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_transactivation-domain-tad.mdx'

word: 'transactivation-domain-tad'

---

<a id="transactivation_domain_tad">Transactivation Domain, TAD</a> - A domain of a [transcription factor](#transcription_factor_tf) that interacts with the [transcriptional](#transcription) machinery, cofactors, and/or [chromatin](#chromatin) modifying machinery (eukaryotes only) in order to facilitate formation of the [transcriptional initiation complex (TIC)](#tight_junction).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_transcription.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'transcription'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['transcription' ,'rna' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'promoter' ,'mrna' ,'protein' ,'translation']
linkedFrom: ['activator','antisense_sequence','crick_strand','enhancer','euchromatin','lux_system_luxi_luxr','machine','modrna','negative_autoregulation','rna_binding_protein_rna_bp','rna_polymerase_rna_p','rna_seq','reporter','rtpcr','tale_taler_talen','terminator','transactivation_domain_tad','transcription','transcription_factor_tf','transcriptional_fusion','transcriptional_fusion','transcriptional_fusion','transcriptional_fusion','transcriptional_fusion','transcriptional_fusion','untranslated_region_utr','2a_linker']
---

<a id="transcription">Transcription</a> - [Transcription](#transcription) is the process of creating an [RNA](#rna) transcript based on information in [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid). A [promoter](#promoter) drives [transcription](#transcription) and decides when and how much transcript is made. The transcript or resulting [mRNA](#mrna) is then transformed into a [protein](#protein) in a process called [translation](#translation).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_transcription-factor-tf.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'transcription-factor-tf'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['protein' ,'promoter' ,'enhancer' ,'transcription' ,'tad' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'molecule' ,'hormone']
linkedFrom: ['ahl','allosteric_regulation','ligand','motif','multimer','operator','rna_polymerase_rna_p','regulatory_element','timescale_separation','transactivation_domain_tad','zinc_finger_zf']
---

<a id="transcription_factor_tf">Transcription Factor, TF</a> - A [protein](#protein) that binds operator sequences in the [promoter](#promoter) or [enhancer](#enhancer) regions distal from the [promoter](#promoter). Activates or represses [transcription](#transcription) depending on the presence of a [trans-activation](#tad) or trans-repression domain, respectively. Also can contain a signal-sensing domain, which allows for external regulation of [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid)\-binding or cellular localisation, *exempli gratia* by small [molecules](#molecule) or [hormones](#hormone).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_transcriptional-fusion.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'transcriptional-fusion'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['transcription' ,'promoter' ,'gene' ,'cleavage' ,'rna' ,'translational_fusion']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="transcriptional_fusion">Transcriptional Fusion</a> - A mechanism for generating several [transcripts](#transcription) from the same input. For example, using the same [promoter](#promoter) for different [genes](#gene) causes all of the [genes](#gene) to be [transcribed](#transcription) if the appropriate input is present. Several [transcripts](#transcription) can sometimes also be produced if processing of a single [transcript](#transcription) creates several, *exempli gratia* if there is a self-[cleaving](#cleavage) [RNA](#rna) element in the [transcript](#transcription). These [transcripts](#transcription) are produced in equal amounts, but can contain different information. See [Translational Fusion](#translational_fusion).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_transcriptome.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'transcriptome'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['rna' ,'cell' ,'dnaMicroarray' ,'rna_seq']
linkedFrom: ['rna_seq']
---

<a id="transcriptome">Transcriptome</a> - Refers to the set of all [RNA](#rna) molecules produced and contained by one [cell](#cell) or population of [cells](#cell).

 Transcriptomes can be studied and built by [DNA microarray assays](#dnaMicroarray) and [next-gen sequencing](#rna_seq) such as [RNA seq](#rna_seq).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="transduction">Transduction</a> - Viral transfer of DNA to new host.

<a id="transfection">Transfection</a> - The process of introducing new genetic material into [cells](#cell), mostly used when talking about [mammalian](#mammal) cells (similar to [transformation](#transformation) in [bacteria](#bacteria)).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

word: 'transformation'

---

<a id="transformation">Transformation</a> - The process of introducing new genetic material into cells, mostly used when talking about [bacterial](#bacteria) cells (similar to [transfection](#transfection) in [mammalian](#mammal) cells). Transformation can be performed by electrical and or chemical means, *exempli gratia* [electroporation](#electroporation).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_translation.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'translation'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['peptide' ,'protein' ,'amino_acid' ,'enzyme' ,'mrna' ,'ribosome' ,'tRNA']
linkedFrom: ['c_terminus_c_ter','elongation','initiation','mirna','mrna','positive_rna_rna','protein','ribosome','ribosome_binding_site_rbs','sense_sequence','transcription','translational_fusion','translational_fusion','translational_fusion','trna','untranslated_region_utr']
---

<a id="translation">Translation</a> - The process of creating a [peptide](#peptide) i.e. [protein](#protein) (sequence of [amino acids](#amino_acid)). *Exempli gratia* a [protein](#protein) or [enzyme](#enzyme)) based on the sequence of an [mRNA](#mrna). The [ribosome](#ribosome) is the key [enzyme](#enzyme) in this process, which also requires [tRNA](#tRNA)s charged with [amino acids](#amino_acid). [Amino acids](#amino_acid) are linked together through [peptide bonds](#protein).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_translational-fusion.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'translational-fusion'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['protein' ,'translation' ,'mrna' ,'polypeptide']
linkedFrom: ['transcriptional_fusion']
---

<a id="translational_fusion">Translational Fusion</a> - A [protein](#protein) fusion where the two [proteins](#protein) are [translated](#translation) together. The coding sequences of [translationally](#translation) fused [proteins](#protein) are on the same [mRNA](#mrna) and form a single [polypeptide](#polypeptide) chain when [translated](#translation).

<a id="tree">Tree</a> - Any tall plant, including many conifers and flowering plants, as well as extinct lycophytes and sphenophytes.

<a id="trichocyst">Trichocyst</a> - Organelle in ciliates and dinoflagellates which releases long filamentous proteins when the cell is disturbed. Used as a defense against would-be predators.

<a id="tropical">Tropical</a> - Region in which the climate undergoes little seasonal change in either temperature or rainfall. Tropical regions of the earth lie primarily between 30 degrees north and south of the equator.

---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_trna.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'trna'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['rna' ,'amino_acid' ,'protein' ,'translation' ,'nucleotide' ,'antiCodon' ,'codon' ,'mrna' ,'ribosome']
linkedFrom: ['anticodon','codon']
---

<a id="trna">tRNA</a> - Transfer [RNA](#rna). These special [RNA](#rna)s have a particular structure and many chemical modifications. They are charged with [amino acids](#amino_acid); the charged tRNAs are then used in [protein](#protein) synthesis i.e. [translation](#translation). The tRNA has a three [nucleotide](#nucleotide) [anticodon](#antiCodon) loop, which complements a three [nucleotide](#nucleotide) [codon](#codon) on an [mRNA](#mrna) in the [ribosome](#ribosome), enabling the [ribosome](#ribosome) to create a new peptide chain from the sequence of an [mRNA](#mrna).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-

<a id="tube_feet">Tube Feet</a> - Extensions of the water-vascular system of echinoderms, protruding from the body and often ending in suckers. May be used for locomotion and/or for maintaining a tight grip on prey or on the bottom.

<a id="tundra">Tundra</a> - A vast, mostly flat, treeless Arctic region of Europe, Asia, and North America in which the subsoil is permanently frozen. The dominant vegetation is low-growing lichens, mosses, and stunted shrubs.

<a id="turgor_pressure">Turgor Pressure</a> - Force exerted outward on a cell wall by the water contained in the cell. This force gives the plant rigidity, and may help to keep it erect.

fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_two-substrate-enzyme.mdx'

---

<a id="two_substrate_enzyme">Two Substrate Enzyme</a> - An enzyme mechanism refers to the way a reaction occurs, that is the order of binding. Here we consider an enzyme that intakes two different substrates, the reaction can happen in five different ways:

Enzyme with two substrates can have various different mechanisms. Described by the diagrams, also shown the double inverses associated to the reactions and the substrates.

1. Sequential random dependent mechanism.
2. Sequential random independant mechanism.
3. Sequential ordered mechanism.
4. Ping-pong mechanism.
5. Theorell-Chance mechanism.


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_general-biology_t_type-ii-restriction-enzymes.mdx'
letter: 't'
word: 'type-ii-restriction-enzymes'
dictionary: 'biology'
category: 'general-biology'
dataSource: 'original-dereck'

published: true

linksTo: ['restriction_enzyme' ,'cleavage' ,'dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid' ,'enzyme' ,'dna_assembly' ,'overhang' ,'golden_gate' ,'moclo']
linkedFrom: ['']
---

<a id="type_ii_restriction_enzymes">Type II Restriction Enzymes</a> - These [restriction enzymes](#restriction_enzyme) are used to [cleave](#cleavage) double-stranded [DNA](#dna_desoxyribonucleic_acid) in a location that is outside the recognition sequence of the [enzyme](#enzyme). They are particularly useful for [DNA assembly](#dna_assembly), as they enable creating arbitrary [overhang](#overhang) sequences. Commonly used Type IIs [enzymes](#enzyme) include BsaI and BbsI, which are both used in [Golden Gate](#golden_gate) or [MoClo assembly](#moclo).


-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-:-


---
fileName: 'biology_cellular-biology_u_ultrastructure.mdx'
letter: 'u'
